Including Cash in Property Division: The Rule and the Intra-Hanafi Dispute
States the rule and three Hanafi views on cash in division

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the default rule against including cash in real property division and identify the three positions of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani, explaining their thamarah al-khilaf.

Core Idea
Cash in division is prohibited without consent; only necessity for an indivisible building permits it, and then only as a last resort.

When co-owners divide a property that includes both land and a building, they cannot simply use cash to even out shares unless everyone agrees. This lesson unpacks the general prohibition and the exceptional necessity that allows cash, and how the three founding Hanafi imams differed on the method. You will see how each imam's approach affects the practical outcome.

Guided Path
1
State the Default Hanafi Position
Identify the general rule from the matn: dirhams (cash) may not be included in the division of real property without the mutual consent (taradi) of all co-owners. This is the baseline.
2
Recognise the Necessity Exception
Understand that when the property includes an indivisible building, pure in-kind division becomes impossible, necessitating some cash adjustment. This triggers the dispute.
Necessity (darurah) is the only ground for overriding consent.
3
Follow Each Imam's Method
Trace the three reported solutions: (a) Abu Yusuf divides the whole property by value, cash is inherently used; (b) Abu Hanifa divides land by area, then the one receiving the building pays cash to equalize; (c) Muhammad first exchanges courtyard land for the building, and only a remaining surplus is paid in cash.
Compare how each imam minimises cash involvement.
4
Analyse the Role of Necessity
Notice that even in the exceptions, cash is not preferred. Abu Hanifa and Muhammad restrict cash to the exact amount needed to compensate for the building or surplus, while Abu Yusuf's value-based division uses cash from the start.
The common thread: cash is a necessary evil, not a tool for convenience.
5
Determine the Thamarah al-Khilaf
Identify the practical consequence: depending on which imam's view a judge adopts, the co-owners may end up with different shares of land and cash. The mufta bihi today often follows Abu Hanifa or Muhammad to minimise arbitrary cash inclusion.
The default rule remains: no cash without consent; the ikhtilaf only concerns the forced exception.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
( ولا يُدْخِلُ الدّراهمَ في القسمة إلا برضاهم) : أي لا يدخل في قسمة العقار الدراهم إلا بالتراضي، حتّى إذا كان أرض وبناء يُقْسَمُ بطريق القيمة عند أبي يوسف ، وعن أبي حنيفة له أنه يَقْسِمُ الأرض بالمساحة ، فالذي وقع البناء في نصيبه يردُّ على الآخر دراهم حتى يساويه، فيُدْخِلُ الدراهم ضرورة، وعن محمد له أنَّه يَرُدُّ على شريكه من العرصة في مقابلة البناء، فإذا بقي فضل ولا يمكن التسوية فحينئذ يردُّ الفضل دراهم ؛ لأنَّ الضرورة في هذا القدر. لم يكن جاز.
(And he does not include dirhams in the division except with their consent): i.e., he does not include dirhams in the division of real property except with mutual agreement, so much so that if there is land and a building, the building is divided by the method of value according to Abu Yusuf. And from Abu Hanifa it is reported that he (the divider) divides the land by area, and then the one in whose share the building falls pays dirhams to the other to equalize it; thus he includes dirhams out of necessity. And from Muhammad it is reported that he (the one with the building) gives back to his partner from the courtyard in exchange for the building, and if a surplus remains and equalization is not possible, then at that point he returns the surplus in dirhams, because the necessity is to that extent. It was not permissible.
Source pages p. 219

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning the inclusion of dirhams (cash) in the division of jointly owned real property. The matn states a general rule: dirhams may not be included in the division unless all co-owners consent. The commentary then explains the exception when land and an indivisible building are involved. Three positions are reported: (1) According to Abu Yusuf, the building is divided based on its value, which inherently involves cash evaluation. (2) According to Abu Hanifa, the land is divided by area; the co-owner who ends up with the building pays dirhams to the other to compensate for the difference, thus cash enters by necessity. (3) According to Muhammad al-Shaybani, the co-owner with the building gives back part of the courtyard (not cash) in exchange; only if a surplus remains after that adjustment does he pay dirhams for the excess. The consensus is that cash should not be introduced voluntarily, but necessity (e.g., indivisibility of the building) can justify it. The relied-upon position is not explicitly stated here, but later Hanafi works often follow a middle path.

Key Terms
الدراهم (al-darahim): Silver coins acting as money; any cash used to equalize shares in a division.
التراضي (al-taradi): Mutual consent of all parties to include cash in the division.
الضرورة (al-darurah): Necessity, specifically the building's indivisibility, which forces cash compensation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, which of the following best describes the condition under which dirhams can be included in the division of land and a building without the co-owners' prior consent?
A) Whenever the building is physically indivisible.
B) Only when all co-owners agree in writing.
C) Only when the co-owner receiving the building pays cash to the other out of necessity.
D) Never; consent is always required.

Key Takeaway
The default Hanafi position is that cash may not be introduced into a property division without consent; the only exception is necessity (darurah) for an indivisible building, and even then cash is limited to the exact compensation required.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute: Istihqaq After Qisma
Detailed commentary on a matn ruling with an intra-Hanafi dispute and multiple scenarios

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on partition after a third-party claim, distinguish the three scenarios, and apply the relied-upon ruling (mufta bihi) in a practical case.

Core Idea
Partition stands after a claim on an undivided part of one share; the affected party may rescind or claim compensation.

When a third party proves ownership of part of one co-owner's share after partition, the jurists differ on whether the partition becomes void. This lesson unpacks the intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, the three possible scenarios, and the practical choice given to the affected party. By working through the source passage, you will understand why the partition is not automatically invalidated and how compensation is calculated.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core issue
Understand that the dispute is about the validity of a completed partition when part of one co-owner's share is claimed by a third party after the partition. The key terms: istihqaq (claim), qisma (partition), tafsikh (voiding).
The claim must be proven; the passage assumes the claim is established.
2
Map the three scenarios
The passage distinguishes three cases based on what part is claimed: (1) specific part in one or both shares, (2) undivided part in both shares, (3) undivided part in one share. Note the consensus or dispute for each.
The dispute only arises in the third scenario.
3
Trace the positions of the Imams
Abu Hanifa: partition not voided; the affected party chooses rescission or compensation. Abu Yusuf: partition voided. Muhammad: most correct narration with Abu Hanifa.
The compensation calculation is based on the proportion of the claim.
4
Examine the compensation calculation
Using the example: house value 1200, one takes front third (400), other back two-thirds (800). Claim of half of front (200). Common property reduces to 900, each entitled to 450. The affected party may take a quarter of the back (150) to balance.
The calculation uses the principle: if all claimed, half of partner's share; if half claimed, quarter.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The text states 'al-ashahh' (most correct) that Muhammad agrees with Abu Hanifa, and Abu Hafs and Abu Sulayman support this. Thus the operative ruling is Abu Hanifa's: partition stands, option for rescission or compensation.
This is the position for fatwa despite Abu Yusuf's dissenting view.

Source Text

[١]قوله : اعلم أن الاستحقاق ...الخ ; ذكر في «الهداية» : إذا استحق بعض نصيب أحدهما بعينه لم يفسخ القسمة عند أبي حنيفة ، ورجع ع المستحق بحصة نصف ما استحق عليه في نصيب شريكه ، وقال أبو يوسف : يفسخ القسمة، والمراد بالبعض الشائع هو الربع والثلث والخمس، وغير ذلك، أما في استحقاق بعض معين لا تفسخُ القسمة بالإجماع، وإذا استحق بعض شائع في الكلّ بالاتفاق فهذه ثلاثة أوجه : الأول : أن يستحق جزءاً شائعاً من كل الدار. والثاني : أن يستحق جزءاً بعينه. (۱) ذكره أبو حفص، وهو الأصح ، لما ذكر أبو سليمان قول محمد مع أبي يوسف . ينظر : «فتح باب العناية (٢) : ٤٠٦).
If part of the share of one of them is claimed, whether undivided or not, the partition is not voided, and he recovers his proportionate part in the context of mutual oaths in sale when before possession, in accordance with analogy, as known in its place. But after possession, it is contrary to analogy because one of them does not claim anything from the other such that the other denies it, so he would swear, while the other claims. However, we know it in sale by text. In our case here, mutual oaths are contrary to analogy because neither is a claimant, and it is reported in sale after possession contrary to analogy, and it has been established that what is reported contrary to analogy cannot be analogized to other cases, and it cannot be attached via the indication of the text because partition is not in the meaning of sale in some respects or it contains the meaning of segregation and exchange. So one should reflect on the answer. If one of them wants partition after mutual oaths, he does not have that because it is not possible, since it cannot be done except by lot, and the share of one may fall in the side of the other, causing harm. And if one of them produces evidence, it is acted upon; if both produce evidence, the more probative evidence is acted upon. Thus in al-Muhit. (1) Thus in Takmilat al-Bahr: His saying: 'If part is claimed... etc.' means: If a specific part of his share is claimed, the partition is not voided according to Imam [Abu Hanifa], and the claimant recovers half of what was claimed from the share of his partner, while Abu Yusuf says he has the option to void. The form of the case: If one takes the front third of the house, and the other the back two-thirds, and their values are equal, then half of the front is claimed: i.e., half of the front third that fell in the share of one. According to the two parties: If he wishes, he can rescind the partition to avoid the harm of division; if he wishes, he can claim from his partner a quarter of what he holds from the back, because if the entire front had been claimed, he would recover half of what he holds; since half is claimed, he recovers half of half, which is a quarter, by analogy of part to whole. Explanation: The total value of the house is 1,200 dirhams, and with the claim of half of the front third, it becomes clear that the common property between them is 900, so each one's right is 450. (1) Takmilat al-Bahr (8:177). Book of Partition/ Its Definition and Rulings: The share of his partner, and it is voided in some undivided part in the whole. Know that the claim is either in part of the share of one: if it is an undivided part, according to Abu Hanifa it is not voided, and according to Abu Yusuf it is voided, and the most correct (sahih) is that Muhammad is with Abu Hanifa. Its form: They partitioned a house, so the western half fell to one, then the undivided half of this western half was claimed. If it is not voided, the claimant has the option: if he wishes, he can rescind the partition to avoid the harm of subdivision; if he wishes, he can claim from the other a quarter. What remains in the hand of the owner of the front is worth 300, and what is in the hand of the owner of the back is worth 900, so he claims a quarter of what is in his hand, its value 150, so that each receives 450. It is mentioned in al-Inayah: Here there are three scenarios: claim of a specific part in one of the two shares or in both together, and claim of an undivided part in the two shares. In the first, the partition is not voided by consensus; in the remaining, it is voided by consensus; in the third, it is voided according to Abu Hanifa, but he has the choice: if he wishes, he recovers the share of that in the share of his partner; if he wishes, he returns what remains and re-partitions. Thus in al-Fawa'id al-Arifiyyah. [1] His saying: Know that the claim... etc.; it is mentioned in al-Hidayah: If a specific part of one's share is claimed, the partition is not voided according to Abu Hanifa, and the claimant recovers half of what was claimed from the share of his partner, and Abu Yusuf said: The partition is voided. What is meant by undivided part is quarter, third, fifth, etc. As for the claim of a specific part, the partition is not voided by consensus. And if an undivided part of the whole is claimed, by consensus these are three scenarios: first, an undivided part of the entire house is claimed; second, a specific part is claimed. (1) Abu Hafs mentioned it, and it is the most correct, because Abu Sulayman mentioned the saying of Muhammad with Abu Yusuf. See: Fath Bab al-Inayah (2:406).
Source pages p. 224

Commentary
This passage is an extended intra-Hanafi dispute concerning the effect of a third-party claim (istihqaq) on a completed partition (qisma). The core issue: if a third party successfully claims ownership of part of one co-owner's share after the partition, does the partition become void? The matn states the general rule: if part of a share is claimed—whether specific or undivided—the partition is not voided, and the affected party recovers proportionately from his partner's share. However, the commentary reveals significant disagreement among the founding imams. Imam Abu Hanifa holds that the partition remains valid; the claimant (the co-owner whose share was partially taken) may either rescind the partition (to avoid fragmentation) or claim compensation from his partner's share. The compensation is calculated by taking half of what was claimed from the partner's property. For example, if one co-owner had the front third and the other the back two-thirds (equal value), and half the front third is claimed, the claimant can take a quarter of the back portion. This is derived by analogy: if the entire front had been claimed, he would take half of the back; for half, he takes half of that half. Abu Yusuf disagrees and rules that the partition is voided (tufsakh) because the claim introduces a defect (shuyu') that nullifies the segregation of shares. The text also records the more correct position (al-ashahh) that Imam Muhammad aligned with Abu Hanifa, though some narrations place him with Abu Yusuf. The commentary further categorizes three scenarios: (1) claim of a specific part in one share or both shares—by consensus, partition is not voided; (2) claim of an undivided part in both shares—by consensus, partition is voided; (3) claim of an undivided part in one share—here the dispute arises. The final word indicates that if the partition is not voided, the aggrieved party has a choice: either rescind the entire partition or accept compensation. This ruling is applied analogically to the case of mutual oaths (tahaluf) in sale, with careful distinction because partition involves both segregation (ifraz) and exchange (mubadala), unlike pure sale.

Key Terms
استحقاق (istihqaq): A third-party claim of ownership over part of the partitioned property, proving that the property was actually owned by someone else.
قسمة (qisma): Partition of jointly owned property into separate shares; a contract of segregation and exchange.
تفسخ (tufsakh): The ruling that the partition is voided or rescinded due to the claim.
بعض شائع (ba'd sha'i'): An undivided part (fraction) of a share, e.g., half or one-third.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position in the Hanafi school, what happens when an undivided part of one co-owner's share is claimed after partition?
A) The partition is automatically voided.
B) The partition stands, but the affected co-owner may either rescind or take compensation.
C) The partition is voided only if the claim is for a specific part.
D) The partition is voided only if both co-owners agree.

Key Takeaway
When an undivided part of one co-owner's share is claimed after partition, the partition is not voided per the relied-upon Hanafi view; the affected party may choose rescission or compensation.

When Reclamation Invalidates Division: Sahibayn vs Abu Yusuf
Intra-Hanafi dispute on division validity after property reclaim

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on division validity when a common part of one partner's share is reclaimed and explain the reasoning behind the Sahibayn's view over Abu Yusuf's.

Core Idea
Division remains valid when a common part from one share is reclaimed; only financial adjustment is needed.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah explores an intra-Hanafi dispute: when an external claimant proves ownership of a common (sha'i') portion from one partner's share after division, does the original division become void? Abu Yusuf argues it does, but the Sahibayn (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani) maintain the division holds. We will trace their arguments and understand the practical outcome.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed scenario
Focus on the case where a common (sha'i') part of only one partner's share is reclaimed after the division has already taken place. This is distinct from cases where a specific part or parts from both partners are reclaimed.
The dispute only arises when the reclaimed part is common (undivided) within that one partner's share.
2
State Abu Yusuf's position and proof
Abu Yusuf argues that reclamation introduces a third partner, and the original division without that partner's consent is invalid. The division should be rescinded because the essence of qisma—ifraz (separation)—is lost.
Abu Yusuf equates this to a case where a common part from both shares is reclaimed, which voids the division by consensus.
3
State the Sahibayn's position and proof
The Sahibayn (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) hold that the division remains valid. Their reasoning: the reclaimed part came from only one partner, so the other partner's share is unaffected. The ability to separate (ifraz) is not negated, because the division could have been done initially with such a share. Therefore, only a financial recourse (ruju') is needed.
The text says 'wa lahum' indicating the Sahibayn's view is relied upon.
4
Understand the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf)
Under Abu Yusuf, the division is rescinded; a new division involving all three partners must occur. Under the Sahibayn, the division stands and the affected partner recovers a proportionate share from the other's property.
The arithmetic example in the passage shows how recourse is calculated (e.g., in halves or thirds).
5
Apply the ruling to a simple example
Suppose A and B divide a house 50-50. Later, C proves ownership of 1/4 of A's half (i.e., 1/8 of the whole). Under the Sahibayn, the division is not undone; A must give B compensation equal to 1/8 of the house's value (since A lost that much and B kept his full share).
If the reclaimed part had been from both shares, the division would be rescinded (as per the earlier scenario).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن كان بعضاً معيناً من نصيب أحدهما ، فقد قيل : إنه على الاختلاف، والصحيح أنها لا تفسخ بالإجماع، بل يرجعُ بقسطه في حصة شريكه، كما إذا كانت الدار بينهما نصفين فقسمت ، فاستحق من يد أحدهما بيت هو خمسة أذرع رجع بنصف ما استحق في نصيب صاحبه. وإن كانت أثلاثاً ثلث لأحدهما ، والثلثان للآخر، فاستحق من يدِ صاحب الثُّلُثِ رَجَعَ بِثْلُثي ما استحق من صاحب الثلثين ، وإن استحق من يدِ صاحب الثلثين رَجَعَ بثلث ما استحق. وإن استحق البعض من نصيب كل واحد ، فإن كان شائعاً، فسختِ القسمة، وإن كان معيناً لم يذكر هذه المسألة. فأقول : لا تفسخ القسمة، بل يُجْعَلُ هذا المستحق كأن لم يكن ، فإن كان الباقي في يد كلّ واحدٍ منهما بقدر نصيبه ، فلا رجوع لأحدهما على صاحبه، وإن نقص من نصيب أحدهما يرجع بالحصة، كما إذا كانت الدار نصفين، والمستحق عشرة أذرع خمسة من نصيب هذا، وخمسة من نصيب ذلك، فلا رجوع لأحدهما على صاحبه، وإن كانت أربعة من هذا وستة من ذلك يرجع الثاني على الأول بذراع. وصحت المهاياة : المهايأة مفاعلة من الهيئة، أو من التهيؤ ، فكأن أحدهما )(١) . والثالث : إذا استحق جزءاً شائعاً من نصيب أحدهم. لأبي يوسف له : إن باستحقاق بعض شائع ظهر شريك ثالث لهما، والقسمة بدون رضاه باطلة، كما إذا استحق بعض شائع في النصيبين ، وهذا يعنـي بـطـلان القسمة ؛ لأن باستحقاق جزء شائع ينعدم معنى القسمة، وهو الإفراز؛ لأنه يوجبُ الرجوع بحصته في نصيب الآخرِ شائعاً بخلاف المعين. ولهما : إن معنى الإفراز لا ينعدمُ باستحقاق جزء شائع في نصيب أحدهما ؛ ولهذا جازت القسمة على هذا الوجه في الابتداء. هذا ملخص ما في «الفوائد العارفية».
And if a specific portion from the share of one of them (is reclaimed), it has been said that there is disagreement, and the correct view is that it is not rescinded by consensus, rather he recovers the equivalent in his partner's share, as if the house was between them in halves and divided, and from the hand of one of them a room of five cubits was reclaimed, he recovers half of what was reclaimed from the share of his partner. And if it was in thirds, one third for one and two thirds for the other, and from the hand of the owner of one third something was reclaimed, he recovers two thirds of what was reclaimed from the owner of two thirds, and if from the hand of the owner of two thirds, he recovers one third of what was reclaimed. And if a portion was reclaimed from the share of each one, if it was common (sha'i'), the division is rescinded, and if it was specific (mu'ayyan), this case was not mentioned. I say: The division is not rescinded, rather this reclaimed part is made as if it never existed. If what remains in the hand of each of them equals his share, then there is no recourse of one against the other; and if there is a deficiency in one's share, he recovers the proportionate amount, as if the house was halves, and the reclaimed ten cubits, five from the share of this and five from that, then no recourse; and if four from this and six from that, the second recovers one cubit from the first. And the muhaayah is valid: muhaayah is a mutual form from hay'ah or from tahayyu', so it is as if one of them... And the third (case): if a common part of the share of one of them is reclaimed. For Abu Yusuf: due to the reclamation of a common part, a third partner appears for the two, and division without his consent is invalid, just as if a common part from both shares is reclaimed, and this means the invalidity of the division; because with the reclamation of a common part, the meaning of division (ifraz) is negated; because it necessitates recourse with his share in the other's share in a common way contrary to specific. And for the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad): the meaning of ifraz is not negated by reclamation of a common part from one's share; hence division in this manner is permissible initially. This is a summary from al-Fawa'id al-'Aarifiyyah.
Source pages p. 226

Commentary
This passage discusses the effect of a reclaimed property (mustahaqq) on an already conducted division of a jointly owned property. The focus is on whether the division is rescinded (fasakh) and the mechanism of recourse (ruju'). The author presents three scenarios: 1) When a specific (mu'ayyan) portion from one partner's share is reclaimed, the division is not rescinded by consensus; the affected partner recovers an equivalent portion from the other's share. 2) When a specific portion is reclaimed from both shares, if the reclaimed portion was common (sha'i') the division is rescinded; if specific, the author (commentator) holds it is not rescinded, but they recalculate. 3) When a common part from one partner's share is reclaimed, there is an intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Yusuf argues a third partner emerges and the division becomes void because ifraz (separation) is compromised; the Sahibayn (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) maintain ifraz remains valid, citing that initial division could be done similarly. The relied-upon position (as summarized from Fawa'id al-'Aarifiyyah) is that of the Sahibayn. The commentary follows the order of the matn and clarifies each scenario with arithmetic examples.

Key Terms
استحقاق (istihqaq): Reclamation of property by an external claimant, proving that the property was wrongly taken.
إفراز (ifraz): Separation of shares; the purpose of division is to assign specific portions to each partner exclusively.
رجوع (ruju'): Recourse; the financial compensation that the affected partner receives from the other partner.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon view in this passage, what happens when a common part (sha'i') is reclaimed from only one partner's share after division?
A) The division is rescinded entirely.
B) The division remains valid, and the affected partner recovers an equivalent from the other's share.
C) The division is void only if the third partner objects.
D) The partners must redo the division with all three.

Key Takeaway
When a common part from one partner's share is reclaimed after division, the division stands, and only a financial recourse is required under the relied-upon Hanafi view.

Definition and Ruling of Muhaya'a (Alternating Use)
Defines muhaya'a and its permissibility by istihsan

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define muhaya'a, state its permissibility by istihsan, and identify the Quranic proof cited.

Core Idea
Muhaya'a allows partners to share use of joint property by alternating, validated by istihsan.

This passage defines the Hanafi concept of muhaya'a — the division of usufruct in jointly owned property without dividing ownership. The ruling is permissibility (jawaz) by istihsan, although qiyas would forbid it as an exchange of benefit for like benefit. The commentator explains the linguistic roots, legal definition, and the proof from the Quranic story of Prophet Salih and the she-camel.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal definition
Read the definition: muhaya'a is the division of usufruct (manafi') in joint property that cannot be used while preserving its essence. Note that it does not affect ownership.
It is distinct from division of physical assets (qismat al-ayn).
2
Recognize the ruling and its basis
The ruling is 'sahha' (valid) by istihsan. Qiyas would reject it, but istihsan overrides. Understand why qiyas rejects it: it involves exchanging a benefit for its like, potentially riba.
Istihsan is a Hanafi source permitting departure from qiyas for a stronger evidence.
3
Analyze the proof
The proof is the verse: 'For her the share and for you the share of a known day' (Ash-Shu'ara' 26:155). This shows alternating use of water was permitted, serving as precedent for muhaya'a.
The verse refers to Prophet Salih's she-camel, where shares were assigned by day.
4
Understand the modality differences
Scholars differed on whether muhaya'a is ifraz (division) or exchange depending on the genus and degree of difference in benefit. If same genus with minor difference, it is partly division; if different genera, pure exchange requiring mutual consent.
This affects whether consent of both partners is required for validity.
5
Examine the examples
Examples: alternating days of dwelling in a house, alternating days of a slave's service, each partner using a specific part (upper/lower floor) or specific slave.
These illustrate practical applications of muhaya'a.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : وصحت المهايأة ; بالياء المثناة التحتية، وهي عبارة عن قسمة المنافع في الأعيان المشتركة، لا يمكن الانتفاع بها مع بقاء عينها، ولا ينافيها أنها تجبر عليه إن طلب أحدهما ، وقيل : المهايأة بإبدال الهمزة ألفاً في بعض اللغات، يعني: نوبت بنوبت قرار في سكون دار هذا بعضاً من دار وهذا بعضاً، وهذا علوها وهذا سفلُها أو خدمة عبد هذا يوماً وهذا يوماً كسكني بيت صغير وعبدين هذا هذا العبد والآخر الآخر يهيء الدار ؛ لانتفاع صاحبه ، أو يتهيأ للانتفاع به ، كما إذا فرغ من انتفاع صاحبه. ( في سكون هذا بعضاً من دار وهذا بعضاً، وهذا علوها وهذا سفلُها، أو خدمة عبد هذا يوماً وهذا يوماً) أي خدمة عبد زيداً يوماً، وعمرواً يوماً، كسكني بيت صغير بأن يسكن فيه زيد يوماً، وعمرو يوماً. (وعبدين هذا هذا العبد، والآخرُ الآخر) : أي يخدم زيداً هذا العبد، ويخدمُ عمراً العبد الآخر. : گرفتن دتیل ، التهايؤ جمع على التعاقب، وهو مهموز اللام من الهيأة. لما فرغ من قسمة الأعيان، شرع في بيان قسمة الأعراض، وهي المهايأة لغة، فإنها مشتقة من الهيأة، وهي: الحالة الظاهرة للتهيئ للشيء، والتهايؤ: تفاعل منهما، وهو أن يتواضعوا على أمر فتراضوا به وحقيقة أنّ كلاً منهم يرضى لهيأة واحدة، أو أنّ الشريك الثاني ينتفع به الشريك الأول ، وأمّا شرعاً فهي عبارة عن قسمة المنافع، وأمّا ا  حكمها : فهو الجواز. وأما كيفية جوازها فقد اختلف العلماء فيها، قال بعضهم: إن جرت المهايأة في الجنس الواحد والمنفعة متفاوتة تفاوتاً يسيراً كما في الثياب والأراضي يعتبر إفرازاً من وجه، مبادلة من وجه حتى لا يتضرّر أحدهما عليها، وإن جرت في الجنس المختلف كالدور والعبيد، يعتبر مبادله كل وجه حتى لا يجوز من غير رضائهما. هذا خلاصة ما في «الفوائد العارفية». قوله : صحت ; استحساناً، فأما القياس فيأباها ; لأنها مبادلة المنفعة بجنسها، إذ كل واحد من الشريكين في نوبته منتفع بملك شريكه عوضاً عن انتفاع الشريك بملكه في نوبته، ولكنا تركنا القياس وجوزناها لقوله لة : مَا شِرْبُ وَلَكُمْ شِرْبُ يَوْم معلوم ). كذا في «النهاية». [1] قوله : في سكون هذا ; أي المتهايئين بعضاً يعني موضعاً معيناً من دار مشتركة بينهما، والآخر منهما بعضاً آخر من الدار. كذا في «الفوائد العارفية».
His statement: 'And muhaaya'ah is valid' — with the underdotted ya (i.e., ي), and it is an expression for the division of usufruct in jointly owned entities, which cannot be utilized while preserving their essence, nor does it contradict that it is compelled if one of them requests. And it was said: muhaaya'ah with hamza replaced by alif in some dialects, meaning: turn by turn decision regarding dwelling in a house, this part of a house and that part, this upper part and that lower part, or service of a slave one day and one day, like dwelling in a small house and two slaves, this slave for this and the other for the other. He prepares the house for his partner's benefit, or prepares for benefit from it, as when he finishes from his partner's benefit. (Regarding dwelling this part of a house and that part, this upper and that lower, or service of a slave one day and one day) meaning service of a slave for Zayd one day and for Amr one day, like dwelling in a small house that Zayd dwells in one day and Amr one day. (And two slaves: this slave for this and the other for the other) meaning this slave serves Zayd, and the other slave serves Amr. ... al-tahaayu' is a collective term for alternation, and it is with hamzated lam from hay'ah. When he finished from division of physical entities, he began to explain division of non-physical attributes, which is muhaaya'ah linguistically, for it is derived from hay'ah, which is the apparent state of preparation for a thing, and al-tahaayu' is a mutual form from both, which is that they agree upon a matter and are content with it, and the reality is that each of them is satisfied with a single state, or that the second partner benefits from the first partner's benefit. As for legally, it is an expression for division of usufruct, and as for its ruling: it is permissible. As for the modality of its permissibility, the scholars differed: some said if muhaaya'ah occurs in a single genus and the benefit is slightly uneven, like in clothes and lands, it is considered partial division (ifraz) and partial exchange, so that neither is harmed; if it occurs in different genera like houses and slaves, it is considered pure exchange such that it is not valid without mutual consent. This is a summary from al-Fawa'id al-'Aarifiyyah. His statement: 'valid' by istihsan; as for qiyas, it rejects it because it is an exchange of benefit for its like, since each partner in his turn benefits from the partner's property in exchange for the partner's benefit from his property in his turn, but we left qiyas and permitted it due to His statement (the Prophet's): 'For her the share and for you the share of a known day' (Surah ash-Shu'ara' 26:155). Thus in al-Nihayah. His statement: 'regarding dwelling this part' meaning, the two partners dwell, one in a specific place from a jointly owned house, and the other in another place from the house. Thus in al-Fawa'id al-'Aarifiyyah.
Source pages p. 226

Commentary
This passage defines muhaya'a (alternating use of a jointly owned property) and explains its ruling. Linguistically, muhaya'a is derived from hay'ah (state) or tahayyu' (preparation), indicating that partners prepare the property for each other's use. Legally, it is the division of usufruct (manafi') while the ownership remains joint. The ruling is permissibility (jawaz) by istihsan, although qiyas would forbid it because it involves exchanging the benefit of one's property for the benefit of the partner's property, which is an exchange of like for like (riba). The proof for istihsan is the verse in Surah Ash-Shu'ara' 26:155 (the story of Prophet Salih and the she-camel: 'For her the share and for you the share of a known day'), which indicates alternating days of drinking water. The commentator mentions that scholars differed on the modality: if the items are of the same genus (e.g., both lands) and the benefit difference is minor, it is considered partial ifraz and partial exchange; if different genera (e.g., house vs. slave), it is pure exchange requiring mutual consent. The text also gives examples: partners alternating days of dwelling in a house or using a slave's service, or each using a specific part (upper/lower) or specific slave.

Key Terms
مهايأة (muhaya'a): Division of usufruct in jointly owned property by alternating use or allocating specific parts.
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference; departing from a clear analogy for a stronger evidence or necessity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary evidence for the permissibility of muhaya'a according to this passage?
A) The consensus of the Companions.
B) The Quranic verse about the she-camel's water share.
C) Qiyas on sale contracts.
D) The principle of necessity.

Key Takeaway
Muhaya'a is a permissible method for dividing usufruct of joint property, justified by istihsan and supported by Quranic precedent.

Muzara'ah: Definition and Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Explaining muzara'ah, its invalidity according to Abu Hanifa and validity according to the two companions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the intra-Hanafi dispute on muzara'ah, explain the evidence of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn, and identify the mufta bihi position with its reasoning.

Core Idea
Muzara'ah is valid by fatwa despite Abu Hanifa's objection, due to community practice and prophetic precedent.

In this lesson, we explore the Hanafi school's internal dispute on sharecropping (muzara'ah). Abu Hanifa deemed it invalid due to resemblance to forbidden transactions, while his two disciples validated it based on the Prophet's Khaybar contract and general need. The relied-upon position for fatwa today is that of the Sahibayn, and we will examine the proofs, the legal device for those following Abu Hanifa, and the practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
Define muzara'ah and its legal classification
Identify the contract as a partnership for cultivation in exchange for a share of the produce. Note that Abu Hanifa holds it invalid whereas Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold it valid. This sets the stage for the dispute.
The definition itself is uncontroversial; the dispute is over its legal validity.
2
Examine Abu Hanifa's proof
Identify his primary evidence: the hadith forbidding mukhabarah (synonym for muzara'ah) and the analogy to qafiz al-tahhan (hiring for an unknown measure of the same commodity). Understand why he considers it similar to invalid hire.
Abu Hanifa classifies muzara'ah as an invalid hire contract due to uncertainty (gharar) in the wage.
3
Examine the Sahibayn's proof
Identify their evidence: the Prophet's transaction with the people of Khaybar, analogy to mudarabah (profit-sharing partnership), widespread community practice, and necessity. Understand why they override the hadith prohibition.
The Sahibayn interpret the prohibition as applying only to a specific form or consider it abrogated.
4
Analyze the tarjih (preference)
Determine why the Sahibayn's view is mufta bihi: due to overwhelming need, continuous practice of the ummah, and the principle that custom and need can override a qiyas (as in istisna').
The fatwa is given according to the Sahibayn, even though Abu Hanifa's proof is technically stronger in terms of strict analogy.
5
Identify the legal device (hila) for Abu Hanifa's followers
Learn the device: the worker is first hired with a fixed wage for a fixed term; after the harvest, the landowner gives a share of produce in lieu of the wage owed. This avoids the gharar while achieving the same end.
This hila is permissible by mutual consent, similar to settling a debt.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

بخلاف دفع الغنم والدجاج ودود القزّ معاملة بنصف الزوائد إلى أولاد الإبريسم، فإنّ تلك الزوائد تتولد من العين ؛ لأنه لا أثر هناك للعمل في تحصيلها، فلم يتحقق
شركة.
[٤] قوله : وبه يفتى...الخ ؛ أي بقول الصاحبين الله يفتى ; لحاجة الناس إليها، ولظهور تعامل الأمة بها، والقياس يتركُ بالتعامل، كما في الاستصناع، ثم المزارعة لصحتِها على قول من يجيزها شروط ثمانية ، أشار إليها المصنف له بقوله : بشرط
Book of Muzara'ah. It is a contract of cultivation for a share of the produce, and it is not valid according to Abu Hanifa. ... (He said: 'Book of Muzara'ah' with the first letter zay and the second ra). It is linguistically from cultivation, and planting is called zira'ah. As for in Sharia, it is an expression for a contract of cultivation for a share of the produce; that is, a contract for cultivation in the form of partnership, such that the landowner says: 'I give it to you as muzara'ah,' and the worker says: 'I accept.' Its pillars are offer and acceptance. What is meant by 'produce' is the yield of what is sown in the land of wheat, barley, and the like, and the preposition 'bi' is attached to 'cultivation.' Then know that zira'ah linguistically is from the pattern of mufa'alah, and it is between two parties, but here it is from one side, and this is sufficient. What is meant by mukhabarah is muzara'ah, and al-khabir is the farmer; that is, he who treats the soft land, and it is said: mukhabarah is on one third and one fourth. Then since the produce in the contract of muzara'ah is among the types in which division occurs, muzara'ah was mentioned after division. ... [2] His saying: 'it' meaning muzara'ah, and it is linguistically mufa'alah from cultivation, and in Sharia it is what the author mentioned: a contract of cultivation for a share of the produce. [3] His saying: 'it is not valid' ... and the legal device for its permissibility according to him is that the worker hires himself out for a known wage for a known period, then when the period passes, the owner gives him a share of the produce in exchange for what became obligatory upon him of the wage in the liability of the owner of the seed; this is permissible by their mutual consent just like other debts. Al-Zayla'i said this. [4] His saying: 'al-mukhabarah' from al-khabir, who is the farmer because he treats al-khabar, meaning soft land. And it is said: from al-khibrah, meaning the share. As in al-Kifayah. ... [1] His saying: 'hiring' ... and the evidence that it is hiring is that it is not valid without mentioning the period; that is a characteristic of hire contracts, so it is hiring for a share of its produce, thus it is similar to qafiz al-tahhan. The Prophet (peace be upon him) forbade qafiz al-tahhan, which is that a person hires a man to grind for him a certain amount of wheat for a qafiz of its flour. As in al-Kifayah. [2] His saying: 'thus it is similar' ... that is, he hires an ox to grind wheat for a qafiz of its flour, and this is a major principle through which the corruption of many hire contracts is known, especially in our lands, as mentioned in the chapter on invalid hire. Al-Jalabi said it. [3] His saying: 'and it is valid according to them two, and fatwa is given accordingly' ... because it is narrated that the Prophet (peace be upon him) made a contract with the people of Khaybar on half of what comes out of dates or crops; and because it is a partnership contract between capital and labour, so it is permissible by analogy to mudarabah, and the common element is fulfilling need, for the owner of capital may not find the work, and the physically capable may not have the capital, so need arises for this contract between them. Unlike giving sheep, chickens, or silkworms as a mu'amalah for half of the increase to the young, for those increases are generated from the substance itself because labour has no effect in obtaining them, so partnership is not realized. [4] His saying: 'and fatwa is given according to them' ... i.e., fatwa is given according to the statement of the two companions (may Allah be pleased with them) due to people's need for it, due to the apparent practice of the ummah with it, and analogy is abandoned due to practice, as in istisna'. Then for the validity of muzara'ah according to those who permit it, there are eight conditions, which the author indicated by his saying: 'provided that...'
Source pages p. 228

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute on the validity of muzara'ah (sharecropping). The author defines muzara'ah as a contract for cultivation of land in exchange for a share of the produce. Abu Hanifa holds it invalid because it resembles prohibited qafiz al-tahhan (hiring for an unknown measure of the same commodity) and due to the hadith prohibiting mukhabarah which is synonymous. However, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad consider it valid based on the Prophet's practice with Khaybar, widespread need, and analogy to mudarabah (profit-sharing partnership). The fatwa is given according to the two companions. The passage also provides a legal device (hila) for those who follow Abu Hanifa: hire the worker with a fixed wage for a fixed term, then after harvest give him a share in lieu of the wage owed. The main issue is that Abu Hanifa classifies it as an invalid hire (ijara fasida) while the Sahibayn see it as a valid partnership. The text also distinguishes muzara'ah from similar contracts involving animals or silkworms where labour is not effective.

Key Terms
المزارعة (al-muzara'ah): A contract for cultivation of land in exchange for a share of the produce, typically between a landowner and a worker.
المخابرة (al-mukhabarah): A synonym for muzara'ah, derived from al-khabir (farmer) or al-khibrah (share). The Prophet forbade it.
قفيز الطحان (qafiz al-tahhan): A prohibited transaction where a person hires a miller to grind grain for a fixed measure of its flour, leading to uncertainty (gharar).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon opinion in the Hanafi school, what is the ruling of muzara'ah (sharecropping)?
A) It is invalid (batil) because it resembles qafiz al-tahhan.
B) It is valid (sahih) if it fulfills certain conditions, based on the practice of the Prophet at Khaybar.
C) It is valid only if the worker is hired with a fixed wage first and then given a share later.
D) It is completely prohibited due to the hadith against mukhabarah.

Key Takeaway
Muzara'ah is valid according to the relied-upon Hanafi position (Sahibayn) due to need and prophetic practice, despite Abu Hanifa's objection.

The Six Conditions of Muraba'ah and Invalidating Stipulations
Explains six conditions of muraba'ah and stipulations that invalidate the contract

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the six conditions of a valid muraba'ah contract and identify stipulations that cut the partnership, rendering the contract fasid.

Core Idea
Any stipulation that cuts the essential partnership in the produce renders the muraba'ah contract void.

Muraba'ah (sharecropping) is a contract where one party provides land and the other labor, with produce shared as agreed. The Hanafi school requires six conditions to prevent dispute and ensure the partnership is genuine. Certain stipulations, like guaranteeing a fixed amount to one party, destroy the partnership and invalidate the contract. This lesson unpacks those conditions and the invalidating stipulations, with the underlying reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the six conditions
List the six conditions mentioned at the beginning: (1) owner of the seed, (2) its type, (3) the share of the other party, (4) vacating the land for the worker, (5) partnership in the produce, and (6) the time for cultivation (if specified).
Condition (6) is implicit from the discussion on time.
2
Understand the rationale for each condition
The subject matter differs based on who provides seed. If the worker provides seed, the contract is for the benefit of the land; if the landowner provides seed, it is for the benefit of the worker. This must be clarified to avoid ignorance (jahalah) leading to dispute. The share of the non-seed provider is essentially their wage, so it must be known. Partnership in the produce is the ultimate purpose.
This is a talil (reason-based) argument.
3
Identify the invalidity principle
Any stipulation that cuts the partnership in the produce (sharika fil-kharij) makes the contract fasid. This is because the contract is initially a hire (ijarah) and ends as a partnership; cutting the partnership defeats the purpose.
4
Apply the principle to specific invalidating stipulations
The passage lists examples: fixed measure for one, produce from a specific area, seed owner taking back the seed, deducting fixed kharaj (wazifah), and allocating straw to one and grain to another. Each eliminates the partnership in the entire produce or a portion, making it void.
5
Distinguish permissible stipulations
Proportional kharaj (muqasamah, e.g., 1/4) or a common share (shayi') like 'one tenth for the landowner' does not invalidate because it does not cut the partnership; it preserves a fractional share in the whole.

Book of Sharecropping / Its Definition and Conditions. And (conditions): owner of the seed, its type, the share of the other party, vacating the land for the worker, and partnership in the produce. 4. Owner of the seed. 5. Its type. 6. The share of the other. And vacating between the land and the worker. And partnership in the produce. If a time is specified in which cultivation is not possible, the cultivation becomes corrupt, so its mention and non-mention are the same. Similarly, if a period is specified after which one of them usually does not live, because it becomes in the meaning of conditioning the contract after death. Thus in 'al-Kifayah'. [1] His saying: And owner of the seed ... because the subject matter of the contract differs by its difference. For if the seed is from the worker, the subject matter is the benefit of the land; if from the landowner, the subject matter is the benefit of the worker. So the subject matter must be clarified, since ignorance leads to dispute. Thus in 'al-Kafi'. (2) His saying: And the share of the other ... i.e. the portion of the one who does not provide seed, because it is the wage for his work or his land, so it must be known. Thus in 'Hashiyat al-Jalabi'. [3] His saying: And partnership in the produce i.e. at its occurrence, because it is the intended purpose. So the contract is initially a hire, and becomes a partnership at the end. Whatever cuts this partnership is corrupting for the contract. This is supported by the branching in his saying: Then it becomes void if one stipulates ... etc. Thus in 'al-Jalabi'. [4] His saying: And partnership in the produce means that a specific amount should not be stipulated for one of them, because it is possible that the land produces only that amount, so there remains no partnership on that estimation, and the condition of partnership requires its continuation. Thus in 'al-Kifayah'. (1) Even if a condition is stipulated in the contract that nullifies vacating, such as the landowner's knowledge of the palm trees with the sharecropper or sale by the worker, it is not permissible. See: 'al-Muhit' (p. 64). (2) 'al-Kifayah' (8:386). (3) 'Dhakhirat al-Uqba' (p.566). (4) 'Dhakhirat al-Uqba' (p.566). (5) 'al-Kifayah' (8:387). Then it becomes void if one stipulates: for one of them a specified measure (qafizan musamma), or what comes out from a specific place, and for the other what comes out from another place, or the owner of the seed takes back his seed, or takes back the kharaj and half of the remainder, or the straw for one and the grain for the other, or [1] His saying: If one stipulates ... i.e. if they stipulate for one of them a specified measure, it is void because by it the partnership is cut; for the land may not produce except that amount, and it becomes like stipulating a fixed number of dirhams for one in mudarabah. Thus in 'al-Hidayah'. (1) [2] His saying: Or the seed owner takes back his seed ... i.e. if they stipulate that the seed owner takes back his seed and the remainder is shared half-half, it is void because it leads to cutting the partnership in some specific part or in all, if only the amount of the seed is produced. Thus in 'al-Hidayah' (2). [3] His saying: Taking back the kharaj; i.e. if they stipulate taking back the kharaj, the land being kharaji land, and that the remainder is between them, it is also void. Unlike if the seed owner stipulates a tenth of the produce for himself or for the other and the remainder between them, because it is a specified common share (shayi'), so it does not lead to cutting the partnership. Thus in 'al-Hidayah' (3). [4] His saying: Or the straw ... i.e. if one stipulates the straw and the other the grain, it is also void because it may be that an affliction strikes, so the grain does not form and only straw comes out. Thus in 'al-Hidayah' (4).
Source pages p. 231

Commentary
This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya is a commentary on the conditions of the muraba'ah (sharecropping) contract and the stipulations that invalidate it. The passage first lists six conditions: (1) identifying the owner of the seed, (2) its type, (3) fixing the share of the other party, (4) vacating the land for the worker, (5) partnership in the produce. The conditions are explained: the subject matter of the contract varies depending on who provides the seed. If the worker provides seed, the contract is for the benefit of the land; if the landowner provides seed, the contract is for the benefit of the worker. Ignorance of these leads to dispute, so they must be known. The share of the other party is essentially the wage for work or land, so it must be specified. Partnership in the produce is the purpose; the contract is initially a hire (ijara) but becomes a partnership (sharika) at the end. Any condition that cuts this partnership invalidates the contract. For example, if a specific fixed amount is stipulated for one party, or produce from a specific area, or the seed owner taking back his seed, or taking back the kharaj (land tax) and dividing the remainder, or allotting straw to one and grain to another—all these eliminate the essential partnership. However, if the kharaj is a proportional share (like 1/4 or 1/5), it does not invalidate because it does not cut the partnership. Similarly, stipulating a tenth of the produce as a common share (shayi') is permissible. The reasoning is based on preventing dispute and preserving the partnership intended.

Key Terms
مزارعة (muzāra‘ah): A sharecropping contract where one party provides land and the other labor, with profit sharing from the produce.
بذر (badhr): Seed; whose property it is determines the subject matter of the contract.
شركة (sharika): Partnership in the produce; the intended purpose of the contract.
خراج (kharāj): Land tax; if fixed, stipulating its removal and then sharing the remainder cuts partnership, invalidating the contract. If proportional (like 1/4), it does not cut partnership.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a muraba'ah contract, why does stipulating a fixed measure (qafizan musamma) for one party invalidate the contract?
A) Because it leads to gharar (uncertainty) in the seed type
B) Because the land might not produce that amount, thus cutting the partnership
C) Because it makes the contract a sale of produce before it exists
D) Because it violates the condition of vacating the land

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school requires that in muraba'ah, the partnership must be preserved in the total produce as a proportional share; any stipulation that fixes a share or allocates different produce types invalidates the contract.

Invalidating Conditions in Muzara'ah (Sharecropping)
Lists six invalidating conditions with commentary from Al-Hidayah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the six conditions that invalidate a muzara'ah contract and explain why each breaks the required partnership.

Core Idea
Any condition that guarantees a fixed amount or specific produce to one party invalidates the sharecropping contract because it destroys the partnership.

In Hanafi fiqh, a muzara'ah contract is fundamentally a partnership (shirkah) in the produce. Therefore, any stipulation that allocates a fixed quantity or isolates a portion of the yield to one party before the harvest contradicts the essence of the contract. This passage from the commentary on Al-Hidayah enumerates six such conditions and explains the reasoning behind each. Understanding these conditions helps you distinguish valid sharecropping agreements from invalid ones.

Guided Path
1
Identify the six conditions
From the passage, list all six stipulations that render the contract invalid. They include fixed measures, specific spots, recovery of seed, removal of kharaj, and allocation of straw vs grain.
The conditions are explicit in the Arabic commentary.
2
Determine how each breaks partnership
For each condition, identify which aspect of partnership (e.g., sharing actual harvest, sharing risk) is disrupted. For example, a fixed measure guarantees a quantity regardless of yield.
The key is that partnership requires sharing in the actual output, not a predetermined share.
3
Understand the proof via analogy
The commentator compares stipulating a fixed measure in muzara'ah to stipulating a fixed sum in mudarabah. Both destroy the partnership nature of the contract.
This qiyas (analogy) is the rational proof used by Hanafi scholars.
4
Note the exception for proportional kharaj
If the kharaj (land tax) is proportional (like 'ushr or muqasamah), stipulating its removal does not invalidate because it does not fix a specific amount before harvest.
Only fixed (muwazzaf) kharaj leads to invalidity.
5
Recognize cross-madhhab difference
Other schools may allow some of these conditions, but Hanafis strictly require partnership. This ikhtilaf is based on different conceptualizations of muzara'ah.
The Hanafi position prioritizes avoiding gharar (uncertainty) through genuine sharing.

[٢] قوله : أو رفع ربّ البذر بذره....الخ ؛ يعني إذا شرطا أن يرجع صاحب البذر بذره، ويكون الباقي بينهما نصفين ؛ لأنه يؤدّي إلى قطع الشركة في بعض معين أو في جميعه، بأن لم يخرج إلا قدر البذر. كذا في «الهداية». [٣]قوله : رفع الخراج ؛ يعني إذا شرطا رفع الخراج، والأرض خراجية، وأن يكون الباقي بينهما فهي باطلة أيضاً، بخلاف ما إذا شرط صاحب البذر عشر الخارج لنفسه أو للآخر ، والباقي بينهما ؛ لأنه معيّن مشاع ، فلا يؤدّي إلى قطع الشركة. كذا في «الهداية». [٤]قوله : أو التبن...الخ ؛ أي إذا شرط لأحدهما التبن والآخـر الحـب، فتبطل أيضاً ؛ لأنه عسى تصيبه آفة، فلا ينعقد الحبّ، ولا يخرج إلا التبن. كذا في «الهداية».
Then it becomes invalid if they stipulate: a specified measure for one, or what comes out from a specific spot for one and from another spot for the other, or the owner of the seed takes back his seed, or the removal of the kharaj and dividing the remainder, or the straw for one and the grain for the other, or dividing the grain and straw for other than the owner of the seed, because it is contrary to the requirement of the contract, or dividing the straw and grain for one of them, because it cuts the partnership in what is intended.
Source pages p. 232

Commentary
This is a ruling passage from the commentary on Al-Hidayah listing conditions that invalidate a muzara'ah (sharecropping) contract. The core principle is that any condition that breaks the partnership (shirkah) between the parties—by allocating a fixed amount or specific produce to one party regardless of actual output—renders the contract void. The commentary elaborates: stipulating a fixed measure of grain (qafzan musamma) is like stipulating a fixed sum in mudarabah; it breaks partnership because the land may not yield that much. Similarly, stipulating that one party gets produce from one spot and the other from another spot is invalid because it predetermines shares based on location, not actual yield. If the seed owner recovers his seed upfront, the contract is invalid because if nothing grows beyond the seed, the other party gets nothing. Stipulating removal of kharaj (land tax) and dividing the remainder is invalid only if kharaj is a fixed tax (mawzuf); if it is a proportional tax (muqasamah) like one-fourth or one-fifth, it does not invalidate because it does not disrupt partnership. Stipulating straw (tibn) for one and grain (habb) for the other is invalid because a blight could destroy the grain, leaving only straw, thus cutting the partnership in the main produce. The same applies to stipulating all straw and grain for one party. Each condition is traced to Al-Hidayah as proof.

Key Terms
مزارعة (muzāra‘ah): A contract of sharecropping where one party provides land and/or seed, and the other provides work, with a share of the produce.
قفزان مسماة (qafzān musammāh): A specified, fixed measure of grain (by volume, e.g., qafiz) promised to one party regardless of actual yield.
خراج (kharāj): Land tax imposed on agricultural land; here distinguished between fixed tax (muwazzaf) and proportional tax (muqāsamah).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does stipulating that the seed owner recovers his seed upfront invalidate the muzara'ah contract according to Hanafi fiqh?
A) Because it involves riba (usury)
B) Because it could reduce the other party's share to zero if only seed grows
C) Because it is a form of gambling (maysir)
D) Because it creates uncertainty (gharar) about the seed quality

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, a muzara'ah contract must preserve partnership in the actual produce; any condition that guarantees a fixed quantity or specific item to one party invalidates it.

Valid and Invalid Conditions in Muzara'ah
Ruling with proof: clarifies valid/invalid conditions in muzara'ah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish valid from invalid conditions in a muzara'ah contract by analyzing asset distributions and the nature of stipulations.

Core Idea
A condition that aligns with the contract's purpose is valid; any distribution creating uncertainty or riba invalidates it.

In this passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah, the commentator clarifies which conditions in a muzara'ah contract preserve its validity and which render it invalid. The key principle is that conditions must not conflict with the contract's essential purpose or introduce forbidden elements like gharar or riba. We will examine the rulings on grain and straw ownership and various asset splits.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling for each condition
Determine whether the stated condition makes the contract valid (sahih) or invalid (batil).
2
Analyze the rationale for valid conditions
For valid conditions, explain why they are consistent with the contract's requirement (e.g., seed owner taking growth).
The condition is muktada al-'aqd – it does not alter the contract's essence.
3
Examine the ikhtilaf on straw
Note the difference between the dominant view (straw follows grain) and the Balkh view (shared by custom).
This is an intra-Hanafi disagreement.
4
Identify the invalid asset distributions
List the specific splits that render the contract invalid, such as land+ox vs seed+labor.
These cases involve uncertainty or riba.
5
Apply the underlying principle
Connect the invalid cases to the general prohibitions of gharar and riba in exchange contracts.
The invalid structures resemble a hire of ox for unknown wage or an uncertain exchange.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن شرط تنصيف الحب والتبن لصاحب البذر ، أو لم يتعرض للتبن صحت) ؛ لأنَّ في الأوَّلِ الشَّرط مقتضى العقد، فإنه نماءُ ملكه، وفي الثاني الشركة فيما هو المقصود حاصلة، وحينئذ التبن لصاحب البذر ، وعند البعض مشترك) تبعاً للحب. [١]قوله : عند البعض مشترك ؛ والبعض هم مشايخ بلخ، وإنما يكون مشتركاً عندهم، اعتباراً للعرف فيما لم ينص عليه المتعاقدان ؛ ولأنه تبع للحب، والتبع يقوم بشرط الأصل. ( وكذا لو كانتِ الأرض والبذرُ لزيد والبقر والعمل لآخر، أو الأرض، أو العمل له ، والبقية لآخر. وبطلت لو كانت الأرض والبقر لزيد، أو البذر والبقر له، والآخران للآخر، أو البذر له والباقي لآخر،
So if they stipulate dividing the grain and straw for the owner of the seed, or they do not mention the straw, then the contract is valid; because in the first, the condition is consistent with the contract's requirement, and in the second, partnership in what is intended occurs. Then the straw belongs to the owner of the seed, and according to some, it is shared following the grain. Likewise, if the land and seed belong to Zayd and the ox and labor to another, or the land or labor to him and the rest to another, it is valid. And it is invalid if the land and ox belong to Zayd, or the seed and ox to him and the other two to the other, or the seed to him and the rest to another.
Source pages p. 233

Commentary
This passage from the commentary outlines both valid and invalid conditions. First, it states that stipulating that all produce (grain and straw) go to the owner of the seed is valid because it is merely the growth of his property; the contract then effectively becomes an employment contract (ijarah) for labor, not a partnership. If the contract is silent about straw, the contract is valid, and the straw follows the grain (i.e., each gets straw proportionally). However, some scholars (mashayikh of Balkh) hold that straw is shared according to custom, since it is a subsidiary of grain. The passage then gives examples of asset distribution: if one party provides land and seed, and the other provides ox and labor, the contract is valid because the first provides capital and the second work. If one provides land and the other provides seed, ox, and labor, it is also valid. However, if the assets are divided in a way that creates uncertainty or riba, such as one providing land and ox and the other providing seed and labor, or one providing seed and ox and the other providing land and labor, or one providing seed and the remaining assets to the other, the contract is invalid. These latter cases involve potential riba (e.g., exchange of labor for seed) or hire of ox for unknown wage.

Key Terms
تبن (tibn): Straw, the byproduct of grain; its ownership is subsidiary to the grain.
مشايخ بلخ (mashāyikh Balkh): A group of later Hanafi jurists from Balkh who held that straw is shared based on customary practice.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the dominant Hanafi position in this passage, if a muzara'ah contract is silent about straw, who does the straw belong to?
A) The worker
B) The seed owner
C) It is shared according to custom
D) The landowner

Key Takeaway
In muzara'ah, conditions that align with the contract's purpose (e.g., seed owner takes produce) are valid; distributions that create uncertainty or riba (e.g., land+ox vs seed+labor) are invalid.

The Seven Combinations in Muzara'ah
Classifies the seven possible combinations in muzara'ah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the seven possible distributions of the four essential elements in muzara'ah and state which are valid and which are invalid according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Only two one-party forms are valid: land-only or labor-only; seed-only and ox-only are invalid.

Muzara'ah (sharecropping) requires a combination of four essential elements: land, seed, labor, and ox. This passage from a Hanafi commentary enumerates the seven rational possibilities, focusing on the permutations where one party contributes exactly one element. The Hanafi school provides clear rulings on each, rooted in the prohibition of riba (usury) and gharar (uncertainty).

Guided Path
1
Identify the four essential elements
List the four elements that must be present in any muzara'ah contract: land (الارض), labor (العمل), seed (البذر), and ox (البقر).
These are the building blocks for the classification.
2
Understand the rational division
The seven types come from distributing these four elements between two parties. The passage focuses on the subset where one party provides exactly one element and the other provides the remaining three. There are four such permutations.
The other three types (all from one, two and two, etc.) are implied but not detailed here.
3
Memorize the rulings for each permutation
Learn that the first two (land from one party or labor from one party) are valid (جائز). The third (seed from one party) is invalid (لا جائز) due to possible riba. The fourth (ox from one party) is also invalid as it constitutes hiring an ox for an unknown wage.
Use mnemonic: Land and Labor are valid; Seed and Ox are invalid.
4
Understand the rationale for invalidity
Seed alone: the seed owner bears risk of loss but may gain an uncertain share, resembling riba. Ox alone: the ox owner receives a share of the crop as payment, but the wage is unknown (gharar).
Both prohibitions aim to eliminate uncertainty and usury.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اعلم أنها بالتقسيم العقلي على سبعة أوجه ؛ لأنه إما أن يكون الواحد من أحدهما، والثلاثة من آخر، وهذا على أربعة أوجه ، وهو إما أن يكونَ الأرض، أو العمل، أو البذر، أو البقر من أحدهما، والباقي من الآخر، والأولان جائزان ، والثَّالثُ لا ؛ لاحتمال الربا، والرابع غير مذكور في «الهداية»، وهو أيضاً غير جائز ؛ لأنه استئجار البقر بأجر مجهول.
Know that according to rational division, there are seven types: because either one of the four items is from one party and the remaining three from the other, and this has four forms: either the land, the labor, the seed, or the ox is from one party and the rest from the other. The first two are permissible, the third is not, due to possibility of riba, and the fourth is not mentioned in Al-Hidayah, and it is also not permissible because it is hiring an ox for an unknown wage.
Source pages p. 233

Commentary
This is a foundational passage from the commentary enumerating the seven possible ways to distribute the four essential elements of muzara'ah—land, seed, ox, and labor—between two parties. The seven types are derived rationally: one party provides all four and the other provides nothing (that is a hire, not muzara'ah—not discussed), or three and one, or two and two, or two and two, etc. The passage focuses on the four permutations where one party provides exactly one item and the other provides the remaining three. The rulings are: (1) If one party provides the land alone and the other provides the seed, ox, and labor, it is valid (this is the standard muzara'ah). (2) If one provides labor alone and the other provides land, seed, and ox, it is also valid (the worker is essentially a laborer). (3) If one provides seed alone and the other provides land, ox, and labor, it is not valid because the seed owner is bearing the risk of loss (if crop fails) while the other gets the produce, resembling riba (exchange of seed for a share in an uncertain crop). (4) If one provides the ox alone and the other provides land, seed, and labor, this is not explicitly mentioned in Al-Hidayah, but it is also invalid because it constitutes hiring the ox for an unknown wage (the share of produce). This classification helps students understand the boundaries of valid muzara'ah.

Key Terms
بقر (baqar): Ox or cattle used for plowing, considered one of the four essential elements in muzara'ah.
أرض (ard): Land, the primary asset in muzara'ah.
عمل (amal): Labor or work involved in cultivation.
بذر (badhr): Seed used for sowing.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi classification in Al-Hidayah, which of the following one-party contributions makes a muzara'ah contract invalid?
A) One party provides the land, the other provides seed, ox, and labor
B) One party provides the seed, the other provides land, ox, and labor
C) One party provides the labor, the other provides land, seed, and ox
D) One party provides the ox, the other provides land, seed, and labor

Key Takeaway
In muzara'ah, the valid forms are those where one party contributes land alone or labor alone; seed-only and ox-only are invalid due to riba and gharar.

Valid and Void Input Combinations in Sharecropping
Defines sharecropping and outlines the first four input combinations with their validity rulings.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify which of the seven possible input combinations in a sharecropping contract are valid (sahih) and which are void (fasid) according to Hanafi fiqh, and explain the reasoning based on muqtada al-aqd.

Core Idea
Sharecropping is valid only when the seed owner's contribution aligns with the growth of his property; otherwise, the contract is void due to gharar or riba.

The Hanafi school regulates sharecropping (muzara'ah) strictly to prevent ambiguity (gharar) and usury (riba). The key principle is that the contract must reflect that the produce is the growth of the seed owner's property. This lesson examines the first four of seven logical input combinations and the rule that the seed owner's share must correspond to his contribution. We also explore the intra-Hanafi dispute on whether straw (tibn) follows the grain or belongs solely to the seed owner.

Guided Path
1
Define muzara'ah and its core requirement
Understand that sharecropping is a partnership where the produce is grown from the seed of one party. The contract must avoid conditions that contradict its inherent nature (muqtada al-aqd).
2
Identify the seven possible input combinations by rational division
Learn that the four inputs (land, seed, oxen, work) can be allocated in seven ways. The first four involve one party providing one input and the other three.
The text outlines these as four aspects: land, work, seed, or oxen from one party.
3
Apply the rule to determine validity of the first four combinations
Check which combinations are permissible (ja'iz): land from one and remaining from other, and work from one and remaining from other are valid. Seed from one is invalid due to potential riba, and oxen from one is invalid as it is hiring with unknown wages.
The third combination (seed from one) is void because it resembles a loan with uncertain return.
4
Analyze the dispute over straw ownership
When the contract is silent, the relied-upon Hanafi position gives straw to the seed owner. The scholars of Balkh argue it is shared per custom. Understand the reasoning and the tarjih.
Sadr al-Shari'ah supports the dominant view that straw follows the seed owner.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب المزارعة تعريفها وشروطها

تنصيف الحب والتبن لغير رب البذر لأنه خلاف مقتضى العقد، أو تنصيف التبن والحب لأحدهما لقطع الشركة في ما هو المقصود، فإن شرط تنصيف الحب والتبن لصاحب البذر ، أو لم يتعرض للتبن صحت لأن في الأول الشرط مقتضى العقد، فإنه نماء ملكه، وفي الثاني الشركة فيما هو المقصود حاصلة، وحينئذ التبن لصاحب البذر ، وعند البعض مشترك تبعاً للحب. وكذا لو كانت الأرض والبذر لزيد والبقر والعمل لآخر، أو الأرض، أو العمل له ، والبقية لآخر. وبطلت لو كانت الأرض والبقر لزيد، أو البذر والبقر له، والآخران للآخر، أو البذر له والباقي لآخر، اعلم أنها بالتقسيم العقلي على سبعة أوجه لأنه إما أن يكون الواحد من أحدهما، والثلاثة من آخر، وهذا على أربعة أوجه ، وهو إما أن يكون الأرض، أو العمل، أو البذر، أو البقر من أحدهما، والباقي من الآخر، والأولان جائزان ، والثالث لا لاحتمال الربا، والرابع غير مذكور في الهداية، وهو أيضاً غير جائز لأنه استئجار البقر بأجر مجهول.
[١]قوله : عند البعض مشترك والبعض هم مشايخ بلخ، وإنما يكون مشتركاً عندهم، اعتباراً للعرف فيما لم ينص عليه المتعاقدان ولأنه تبع للحب، والتبع يقوم بشرط الأصل.

وإذا صحت ، فالخارج على الشرط ، ولا شيء للعامل إن لم يخرج، ويجبر من أبي عن المضي إلا رب البذر ومتى فسدت فالخارج لرب البذر، وللآخر أجر مثل أرضه، أو عمله، ولا يزاد ما على شرط

(وإذا صحت، فالخارج على الشرط، ولا شيء للعامل إن لم يخرج، ويُجبر من أبى عن المضي إلا رب البذر) لأن المضي عليه لا يخلو عن ضرر، وهو إهلاك البذور، ومتى فسدت فالخارج لرب البذر، وللآخر أجر مثل أرضه، أو عمله، ولا يزاد ما على شرط ، وعند محمد له بالغا ما بلغ.
