Timing of Udhiyah and Conditions of Obligation
Expansion of Hidayah on udhiyah timing and conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruled time for udhiyah, explain the inter-madhhab dispute regarding slaughter before the Eid prayer, and apply the condition that obligation depends on the last day of the period.

Core Idea
The time for udhiyah begins at Fajr of the 10th and ends at sunset of the 13th; obligation is determined by the last day.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya clarifies the precise timing for udhiyah and the conditions that trigger its obligation. It addresses a key dispute with the Shafi'i and Maliki schools regarding whether slaughter is valid before the Imam's Eid prayer. Additionally, it explains how changes in wealth and birth/death affect wajib status, emphasizing that the end of the period is decisive.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi time period for udhiyah
Find the start and end points from the text: after Fajr of the day of Nahr (10th Dhul Hijjah) until shortly before sunset of the third day (13th Dhul Hijjah).
The text uses 'qabil ghubub al-yawm al-thalith' meaning just before sunset of the third day.
2
Contrast the Hanafi view with the Shafi'i/Maliki positions
Note that Shafi'i permits slaughter in four days (adding the 13th as a full day) and both Shafi'i and Maliki require slaughter after the Eid prayer and after the Imam's nahr.
The passage quotes the Shafi'i hadith 'All days of Tashriq are days of slaughter' from Ahmad and Ibn Hibban.
3
Analyze the Hanafi proof and response
Understand the Hanafi reliance on companion statements (Umar, Ali, Ibn Abbas) that the days of Nahr are three, and the rational principle of taking the certain (al-mutaqin) when reports conflict.
The companions stated it as heard (sam'an), indicating it is not personal opinion.
4
Apply the condition related to wealth status at the end of the period
The text states that obligation is determined by the last day: if one is rich at the start but poor at the end, no udhiyah; if poor then rich, it is wajib. Similarly, birth on the last day activates obligation; death removes it.
This is a practical rule for changes during the three days.
5
Consider special cases: traveler, villager, fitna, mistaken day
Note that udhiyah is not wajib on a traveler; a villager (with no Eid prayer) may delay slaughter without concern; if there is fitna and no imam, slaughter after Fajr suffices; if the day was mistaken (Arafah instead of Eid), the sacrifice remains valid.
These illustrate the flexibility within the Hanafi ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

وبعد طلوع فجر يوم النحر إن ذُبِحَ في غيره ، وآخره قبيل غروب اليوم الثالث ، واعتبر الآخر للفقير وضده، والولادة والموت
( وبعد طلوع فجر يوم النحر إن ذبح في غيره، وآخره قبيل غروب اليوم الثالث) ، فالمعتبر في هذا المكان الفعلُ لا مكانَ مَن عليه، لكن الأضحية لا تَجِبُّ على المسافر، كذا في «الهداية ، وعند مالك (۲) له ، والشَّافِعِي (۳) : لا تجوز بعد الصلاة قبل نَحْر الإمام، وتجوز عند الشَّافِعِي (٤٣) له في أربعة أيام.
(1)
(واعتبر الآخر للفقير وضده، والولادة والموت) : أي إذا كان غنياً في أوَّل الأيام فقيراً في آخرها لا تَجِبُّ عليه وعلى العكس تجب ، وإن وُلِدَ في اليوم الآخر تَجِبُّ عليه ، وإن مات فيه لا تَجِبُّ عليه.

ولنا : ما روي عن عمر وعلي وابن عباس أنهم قالوا : أيام النحر ثلاثة أفضلُها أوّلُها ، وقد قالوه سماعاً ؛ لأنَّ الرأي لا يهتدي إلى المقادير، وفي الأخبار تعارض فأخذ بالمتيقن وهو الأقل، وأفضلها أولها كما قالوا ؛ ولأن فيه مسارعة إلى أداء القربة ، وهو الأصل إلا بمعارض. كذا في «الهداية»(۳).
Book of Udhiyah: its definition, conditions, and rulings. And after dawn of the day of Nahr if sacrificed on other than it, and its end shortly before sunset of the third day. And consider the last day for the poor and its opposite, and birth and death. (And after dawn of the day of Nahr if sacrificed on other than it, and its end shortly before sunset of the third day.) So what is considered in this place is the action, not the place of the one upon whom it is? But udhiyah is not obligatory upon the traveler. Thus in al-Hidayah. According to Malik (2) and al-Shafi'i (3): it is not permissible after the prayer before the Imam's nahr. And it is permissible according to al-Shafi'i (4) in four days. (And consider the last day for the poor and its opposite, and birth and death): i.e., if he was rich at the beginning of the days and poor at their end, it is not obligatory upon him; and if the opposite, it is obligatory; and if he was born on the last day, it is obligatory upon him; and if he died on it, it is not obligatory upon him. And there is no meaning for delay in the case of the villager since there is no prayer upon him. And what we narrated is a proof against Malik and al-Shafi'i in their negation of permissibility after the prayer before the Imam's nahr. Thus in al-Hidayah. [1] His saying: And its end shortly before sunset of the third day; and it is said: it is permissible until al-Muharram. And if the Imam prayed, then it became apparent that he prayed without purity, the prayer is repeated without the udhiyah. And if there was fitna in the town and there remained no ruler to lead them in the Eid prayer, and they slaughtered after dawn before the Eid prayer, it suffices them. And if they testified before the Imam that it was the day of Eid and he prayed, then it became clear that it was the day of Arafah, the prayer and udhiyah suffice them. Thus mentioned by al-Zayla'i (6). [2] His saying: And it is permissible according to al-Shafi'i? because of his saying: 'All the days of Tashriq are days of slaughter' narrated by Ahmad in his Musnad and Ibn Hibban in his Sahih from Jubayr ibn Mut'im. And for us: what was narrated from 'Umar, 'Ali and Ibn 'Abbas that they said: The days of Nahr are three, the best of them is the first of them. And they said it by hearing, because opinion does not attain to determinations. And in the reports there is contradiction, so one took the certain, which is the least, and the best of them is the first of them as they said; and because in it there is hastening to perform the act of worship, and it is the principle except where there is a counter. Thus in al-Hidayah (3).
Source pages p. 251

Commentary
This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya is an expansion of the rulings on udhiyah from al-Hidayah. It first defines the time period for sacrifice: from after the Fajr of the day of Nahr (10th Dhul Hijjah) until just before sunset of the third day (13th Dhul Hijjah). The emphasis is on the action (sacrifice) itself, not the location of the person. A traveler is not obligated to perform udhiyah. Then a dispute is mentioned: Malik and al-Shafi'i hold that slaughter before the Imam's prayer is invalid after the prayer, whereas al-Shafi'i also permits it in four days. The Hanafi position, based on narrations from 'Umar, 'Ali, and Ibn 'Abbas, is that the days are three, the best being the first, and slaughter is valid after Fajr even before the prayer. The passage also discusses the case of change in wealth status: obligation depends on the last day of the period. If one was rich at the start but poor at the end, no udhiyah; if poor then rich, it is wajib. Birth of a person on the last day makes udhiyah wajib upon him; death on that day removes obligation. Special cases like absence of an Imam due to fitna or mistaken identification of the day are also addressed, with the ruling that the udhiyah remains valid. The Hanafi proof is based on companion statements considered sam'an (heard) against the Shafi'i hadith of 'all days of Tashriq are slaughter days', which is counterbalanced by taking the certain minimum of three days.

Key Terms
أضحية (uḍḥiyyah): The animal sacrificed on the days of Nahr (10-13 Dhul Hijjah) as an act of worship
نحر (naḥr): Slaughtering a camel by stabbing in the neck; used generically for sacrifice
أيام التشريق (ayyām al-tashrīq): The 11th, 12th, and 13th of Dhul Hijjah

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when does the time for udhiyah begin?
A) After the Eid prayer on the 10th of Dhul Hijjah
B) After Fajr on the day of Nahr (10th Dhul Hijjah)
C) At dawn on the 11th of Dhul Hijjah
D) After the Imam's nahr

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi time for udhiyah is from Fajr of 10th to sunset of 13th; obligation is based on the last day of the period.

The Dislike of Night Slaughter in Udhiyah
Ruling on night slaughter with proof from companions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on night slaughter and explain the reason behind it.

Core Idea
Night slaughter is makruh tanzihi due to risk of error in the darkness.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah explains the ruling on slaughtering an udhiyah at night. The Hanafi school considers it disliked (makruh tanzihi) because of possible mistakes in identifying the slaughter spot or the animal's ownership in the dark. The lesson also presents the proof from the Companions and the reasoning that the first day of Nahr is best.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is slaughtering an udhiyah at night. The ruling is makruh tanzihi (disliked, not prohibited). Note that the dislike applies to the two middle nights only.
2
Find the dalil (proof)
The proof comes from reports of 'Umar, 'Ali, and Ibn 'Abbas that the days of Nahr are three, with the first being best. They said it by hearing (samā‘an), indicating it is a transmitted knowledge, not opinion.
Companion statements are a source of evidence in Hanafi fiqh, though debated in other schools.
3
Understand the illah (reason)
The dislike is due to the possibility of error (iḥtimāl al-ghalaṭ) in the darkness: either missing the correct slaughter spot or confusing one's own animal with another's.
This is a practical consideration, not a textual prohibition.
4
Note the preferred time
The first day of Nahr is the best because it is hastening to perform the act of worship. The minimum certain days are three, hence the first is chosen.
The principle of al-mubādarah (hastening to good deeds) is invoked.

And it is disliked to slaughter at night. If it (the udhiyah) is abandoned and its days have passed, the one who vowed gives in charity (the animal); and the poor person who bought it for udhiyah gives it alive; and the rich person gives its value whether he bought (it) or not. And it is disliked to slaughter at night. If it (the udhiyah) is abandoned: i.e., the udhiyah, and its days have passed, the one who vowed gives in charity; and the poor person who bought it for udhiyah gives it alive; and the rich person gives its value whether he bought it or not. The meaning is that he vowed to sacrifice this sheep, then it is attached to the item; and the poor person it is only obligatory upon him by purchase with the intention of udhiyah; as for the rich, the obligation is in his liability whether he bought the sheep or not. And for us: what was narrated from 'Umar, 'Ali, and Ibn 'Abbas that they said: The days of Nahr are three, the best of them is the first of them. And they said it by hearing, because opinion does not attain to determinations. And in the reports there is contradiction, so one took the certain, which is the least, and the best of them is the first of them as they said; and because in it there is hastening to perform the act of worship, and it is the principle except where there is a counter. Thus in al-Hidayah (3). [1] His saying: And it is disliked to slaughter at night; meaning in its nights, and the intent is the two middle nights only, except that slaughter in the nights is disliked due to the possibility of error in the slaughter spot, or in the sheep whether it is his or someone else's in the darkness of night. Thus in al-Hidayah (3). [2] His saying: The one who vowed gives in charity... etc.: It is that he has a sheep in his possession and says: 'Upon me is to sacrifice (uḍḥi) with this sheep', whether the obligor is poor or rich. And if he vowed to sacrifice but did not specify anything, it falls upon the sheep, and the one who vowed does not eat from it; and if he ate, he must pay the value of what he ate, said al-Jalabi? [3] His saying: The meaning is that he vowed to sacrifice... etc.: The meaning is that if he did not sacrifice until its time passed.
Source pages p. 252

Commentary
This passage continues the commentary on udhiyah, focusing on two issues: first, the dislike of slaughtering at night (makruh tanzihi) because of the risk of errors in identifying the proper slaughter spot or confusion over ownership in the dark. The disliked nights are the two middle nights (of the three days). Second, it addresses what happens if the time for udhiyah passes without the sacrifice having been performed, in cases where one has made a vow (nathr) to sacrifice a specific animal. For a nadhir (one who vowed) who owns a specific sheep and says 'I vow to sacrifice this sheep', if the days pass, he must give the sheep alive in charity. For a poor person who bought a sheep with the intention of udhiyah (the obligation being attached to the purchase), he gives the sheep alive in charity. For a rich person (on whom udhiyah is wajib in the first place), the obligation is in his liability; he must give the value of a sheep in charity, whether he bought one or not. The passage also notes that if one vowed to sacrifice but did not specify an animal, the vow attaches to a sheep that he owns, and he (the nadhir) cannot eat from it; if he does, he must compensate. These rulings are from al-Hidayah and further explained with reasoning from the companions.

Key Terms
كره (kariha): Disliked (makruh) – an act whose omission is rewarded but commission is not punished in Hanafi fiqh.
نذر (nadhara (nathr)): A vow: making an act of worship obligatory upon oneself by a verbal declaration.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It is forbidden (haram) by ijma
B) It is due to the risk of error in the dark
C) It is because the Prophet never slaughtered at night
D) It is disliked only if the animal is not owned

Key Takeaway
Night slaughter is makruh tanzihi due to the risk of error, but it is not invalid or haram.

Rulings for Missed Vowed Sacrifice
Rulings for missed sacrifice after a vow

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the obligations of a poor vs. rich person when a vowed sacrifice is missed, and state the rule regarding eating from a vowed animal.

Core Idea
If a vowed sacrifice is missed, the poor give the animal alive; the rich give its value; and the nadhir cannot eat from it.

This passage continues the commentary on udhiyah, addressing what happens when the days of Nahr have passed without the sacrifice being performed, particularly when a vow (nathr) was made. The ruling depends on whether the person is rich or poor, and it also explains the prohibition on the nadhir (one who vowed) eating from the vowed animal.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
A person vowed to sacrifice a specific animal (e.g., 'I vow to sacrifice this sheep'), but the days of Nahr have passed without the sacrifice.
2
Understand the effect of the vow
The vow attaches the obligation to the animal itself. The animal becomes designated for sacrifice.
This is called ta‘alluq bi al-mahall.
3
Distinguish between poor and rich
For a poor person, the obligation of udhiyah only becomes binding when he purchases the animal with the intention. If missed, he gives the animal alive in charity. For a rich person, the obligation is in his liability (dhimmah) from the beginning; if missed, he gives the value of the animal in charity, regardless of whether he bought one.
The poor person's obligation is 'an al-shirā'; the rich person's is 'an al-dhimmah'.
4
Apply the rule about eating
The nadhir (one who vowed) cannot eat from the sacrificed animal if it had been slaughtered. If he does eat, he must pay the value of what he ate.
This is because the animal is dedicated to Allah.

Ruling on Delaying a Vowed Sacrifice and Required Charity
Ruling with proof: charity substitute for missed vowed sacrifice

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when a vowed sacrifice is delayed past its time and distinguish the obligation for a poor vs. a rich person.

Core Idea
Delaying a vowed sacrifice obligates charity: poor gives the animal alive, rich gives its value.

This lesson explains what happens if a person who vowed to sacrifice a specific animal fails to do so during the three days of Eid al-Adha. The Hanafi school distinguishes between a poor and a rich person: for the poor, the obligation is attached to the animal; for the rich, it is a debt on the liability. The proof comes from a companion saying about the three days.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is delaying a vowed sacrifice past the days of sacrifice. The ruling is that charity becomes wajib.
The original obligation was to sacrifice; now it is substituted by charity.
2
Distinguish between poor and rich
For the poor (who bought the animal intending sacrifice), he must give the animal alive. For the rich, he must give its value, whether he bought it or not.
The obligation for the rich is on his liability (dhimma), not tied to the animal.
3
Locate the dalil
The proof is the saying of Umar, Ali, and Ibn Abbas: 'The days of sacrifice are three, the best is the first.' This establishes the limited time frame.
This is considered hearsay (samā'an) from the Prophet, as opinion cannot determine such quantities.
4
Understand the usul reasoning
Conflicting reports exist about the number of days; the certain minimum (three) is taken. The first day is best because it is hastening to worship.
This follows the principle of taking the certain when reports conflict.
5
Apply the ruling
If a rich person vowed to sacrifice a specific sheep but did not, he must give its value in charity. A poor person who bought it must give the sheep alive.
The charity fulfills the obligation; the sacrifice is no longer possible.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكره الذبح ليلاً، فإن تركت، ومضت أيَّامُها تصدقُ الناذر، وفقير شراها للأضحية بها حية، والغني بقيمتها شراها أو لا. المراد أنه نذر أن يُضَحي بهذه الشَّاة، فإنه حينئذ يتعلق بالمحل، والفقير إنما يجب عليه بالشراء بنية الأضحية، فأما الغنى فالواجب يتعلق بذمته شَرَى الشَّاة أو لا. ولنا : ما روي عن عمر وعلي وابن عباس أنهم قالوا : أيام النحر ثلاثة أفضلُها أوّلُها، وقد قالوه سماعاً؛ لأنَّ الرأي لا يهتدي إلى المقادير، وفي الأخبار تعارض فأخذ بالمتيقن وهو الأقل، وأفضلها أولها كما قالوا؛ ولأن فيه مسارعة إلى أداء القربة، وهو الأصل إلا بمعارض. كذا في «الهداية».
It is disliked to slaughter at night. If she abandons it and its days pass, the vower gives charity: the poor person (if he bought it for sacrifice) gives the animal alive, and the rich person gives its value whether he bought it or not. The meaning is that he vowed to sacrifice this sheep; then it is attached to the specific animal. The poor person only becomes obligated by purchasing with the intention of sacrifice. As for the rich, the obligation is on his liability whether he bought the sheep or not. Our proof is what was narrated from Umar, Ali, and Ibn Abbas that they said: The days of sacrifice are three, the best of them is the first. They said it as hearsay because opinion cannot reach quantities. The reports conflict, so one takes the certain [minimum], which is the fewest. Its best is its first as they said, and because there is haste in performing the act of worship, and that is the principle unless there is an opposing factor. Thus in Al-Hidayah.
Source pages p. 252

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the Hidayah commentary. It addresses the situation where a person has vowed to sacrifice a specific animal (e.g., 'I vow to sacrifice this sheep') and then fails to do so within the three days of Eid al-Adha. The ruling distinguishes between a poor person and a rich person. For the poor person, the obligation is tied to the animal itself; if he purchased it with the intention of sacrifice, he must give the animal away alive as charity. For the rich person, the obligation is a debt on his liability; he must give the value of the animal in charity regardless of whether he bought it or not. The proof cited is the statement of the Companions Umar, Ali, and Ibn Abbas that the days of sacrifice are three, with the first day being best. This is considered hearsay (samā'an) from the Prophet, as such precise quantities cannot be known by opinion. The conflicting reports are resolved by taking the certain minimum (three days).

Key Terms
الناذر (al-nādhir): The person who makes a vow (nadhr) to perform a sacrifice.
التصدق (al-tasadduq): Giving the animal or its value as charity to fulfill the obligation of a missed sacrifice.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Minimum Ages for Sacrificial Animals
Specifies minimum ages for valid udhiyah animals

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the minimum age requirements for each sacrificial animal (camel, cow, goat, sheep) according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
A jadh' sheep (6 months) is valid only from fat-tailed sheep; all other animals must be thani (one year or more).

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah specifies the legally recognized ages for sacrificial animals in the Hanafi school. Knowing these exact ages is crucial for the validity of your udhiyah. The text distinguishes between jadh' (a six-month-old sheep) and thani (older animals), and it restricts the jadh' to a specific type of sheep called da'n (fat-tailed sheep).

Guided Path
1
Identify the animal types
List the three categories: camels, cattle (cows), and sheep/goats (ghanam).
Sheep/goats are subdivided into da'n (fat-tailed sheep) and ma'z (goats).
2
Note the minimum age for each
For camels: 5 years (thani). For cattle: 2 years (thani). For sheep/goats: either jadh' (6 months, only from da'n) or thani (1 year).
Thani is the minimum for camels, cattle, and goats; jadh' is an exception for da'n sheep.
3
Understand the jadh' exception
Jadh' is defined as a sheep that is six months old, but it is only valid if the sheep is da'n (having a fat tail). Goats (ma'z) cannot be sacrificed as jadh'.
This is a Hanafi specific ruling; other schools allow jadh' from goats.
4
Apply to a practical scenario
If someone wants to sacrifice a goat, it must be at least one year old. If they want to sacrifice a fat-tailed sheep, it can be six months old (jadh') or one year old (thani).
Choosing an older animal is recommended but not required.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وصح الجذع من الضأن، والثني فصاعداً من الثلاثة، وهو ابن خمس من الإبل وحولين من البقر وحول من الشاة. الجذعُ شاة لها ستة أشهر، والضأن ما تكون له إلية. والثني فصاعداً من الثلاثة : أي من الشاة أعم من أن يكون ضاناً أو معزا ومن البقر ومن الإبل، وهو ابن خمس من الإبل وحولين من البقر وحول من الشاة.
The jadh' from sheep is valid, and the thaniy and above from the three [types]. It (al-thani) is: from camels: five years; from cattle: two years; from sheep/goats: one year. Al-Jadh' is a sheep that is six months old. Al-Da'n is what has a fat tail. Al-Thani is from the three types: from sheep (whether da'n or ma'z), from cattle, and from camels.
Source pages p. 253

Commentary
This passage states the minimal ages for sacrificial animals. It is a straightforward ruling from the matn. The jadh' (a sheep at least six months old) is valid only from the specific type of sheep called 'da'n' (fat-tailed sheep). For other animals (camels, cattle, and goats), the minimum is 'thani' (ثني): a camel at least five years old, a cow at least two years old, and a goat or ordinary sheep at least one year old. The term 'al-thalathah' (the three) refers to camels, cattle, and sheep/goats. The passage notes that 'da'n' is a sheep with a fat tail (إلية), which is the typical sheep in many regions. This definition distinguishes it from goats (ma'z). The commentary by al-Jalabi explains that the six-month requirement is according to the jurists, whereas linguistically 'jadh' may mean a one-year-old, but the jurists permit six months if the animal is large enough.

Key Terms
الجذع (al-jadh'): A sheep (da'n) that is six months old, permissible for sacrifice.
الثني (al-thani): An animal that has completed a full year (or more) and is at least the age specified: camel 5 years, cow 2 years, goat/sheep 1 year.
الضأن (al-da'n): Sheep that have a fat tail (إلية), distinguishing them from goats.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the minimum age for a cow to be valid for sacrifice according to the Hanafi school?
A) One year
B) Two years
C) Three years
D) Six months

Key Takeaway
For a Hanafi udhiyah, a jadh' sheep (6 months) must be da'n (fat-tailed); all other animals must be at least thani (camel 5y, cow 2y, goat/sheep 1y).

Valid Ages for Sacrificial Animals and Replacement Rulings
Defines valid ages for sacrificial animals and charity obligation when sacrifice is missed.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the minimum ages for sacrificial animals according to the Hanafi school and explain the ruling on charity when the animal is lost or time passes.

Core Idea
A jadha' sheep of six months is valid if large; other animals must be thani. If sacrifice is missed, the rich give value, the poor give the animal itself.

This passage from `Umdat al-Ri`ayah clarifies the age conditions for udhiyah and then addresses a practical scenario: what if the animal cannot be sacrificed? The Hanafi school distinguishes between a rich person who vowed and a poor person who obligated himself by purchasing. Understanding these distinctions ensures proper fiqh application in real sacrifice situations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three animal types and their required ages
The matn states that jadha' from sheep is valid, and thani from three types (sheep/goats, cows, camels). Read the ages: camel 5 years, cow 2 years, sheep/goat 1 year.
Note that 'sheep' in the matn includes both dha'n (sheep with tail) and ma'z (goats).
2
Understand the definition of jadha' and the largeness condition
The commentator explains jadha' is six months according to jurists, but only if it is large enough to be mistaken for a thani from a distance. This is a special Hanafi concession.
Linguistically, jadha' means one year, but fiqh allows six months with size.
3
See how the rule extends to buffalo and crossbreeds
The commentator includes buffalo under 'cows' due to similarity, and crossbreeds follow the mother in age ruling.
This is an application of qiyas.
4
Analyze the charity ruling for rich vs poor when sacrifice is impossible
If a rich person vows a specific animal, he gives its value in charity; if a poor person buys with intention, he gives the specific animal. The passage compares to missing Jumu'ah and praying Zuhr.
The difference is based on whether obligation is on liability (dhimma) or attached to the physical entity.

Book of Sacrifice: Its definition, conditions, and rulings. And the jadha' from sheep is valid, and the thani and above from the three (types), and it is a five-year-old from camels, two-year-old from cows, and one-year-old from sheep. (And the jadha' from sheep is valid), the jadha' is a sheep of six months, and sheep (dha'n) are those with a tail. (And the thani and above from the three: meaning from sheep, whether sheep or goat, and from cows, and from camels, and it is a five-year-old from camels, two-year-old from cows, and one-year-old from sheep). So the rich person, if he vows to sacrifice this sheep – i.e., a specific sheep – he is obligated to give its value in charity, whether he bought it for sacrifice or not, because the obligation is attached to his liability. Likewise, the poor person who has obligated upon himself to buy it for sacrifice, he is obligated to give the specific animal in charity, because it is attached to the physical entity, and hope for drawing near by slaughter has been lost, and the physical entity remains deserving of being spent for Allah, so he is obligated to give the specific animal in charity. And it is only obligatory upon the poor person by purchasing with the intention of sacrifice, because purchasing by the poor person coupled with the intention of sacrifice is like a vow. So if slaughter becomes impossible due to the passing of its time, he must give charity, like Jumu'ah: one prays Zuhr after its time has passed, as stated by al-`Alawi. [1] His statement: 'And the jadha' is valid...' up to his statement: 'from the three' is an indication to explain the types by which sacrifice is not permissible except with them, and a specification of the age below which it is not permissible. Said by al-Jalabi. [2] His statement: 'It has six months...' etc., meaning in the school of the jurists. We only specified this because according to the linguists, jadha' from sheep is one that has completed a year, as in al-Nihaya, but the jurists only allow it at six months if it is large, such that if mixed with thanis, it would be indistinguishable to an observer from a distance. Said by al-Jalabi. [3] His statement: 'and two years from cows' includes buffalo due to similarity, and a crossbreed between domestic and wild follows the mother because she is the origin in following; because it is a part of her; for this reason it follows her in slavery and freedom. This is because what is separated from the male is water, and it is not a locus for this ruling, and from the mother is the animal, and it is a locus, so it is considered. Said by al-Jalabi.
Source pages p. 253

Commentary
This passage from `Umdat al-Ri`ayah is an expansion of the matn of al-Wiqayah on the chapter of Udhiyah (sacrificial animal). It first states the ruling: a jadha' (young sheep of six months) is valid for sacrifice, and the thani (older) and above from three types (sheep, cows, camels) with specified ages. The commentator then explains each term: jadha' is a sheep of six months according to jurists, though linguists define it as one year; the jurists allow it only if it is large enough to be confused with a thani from a distance. The matn's 'from the three' refers to sheep (including both goats and sheep), cows, and camels, with ages: five years for camel, two years for cow, one year for sheep. The commentator then discusses a derived ruling: if a rich person vows to sacrifice a specific sheep, he must give its value in charity if it is lost, because the obligation is on his liability (dhimma). For a poor person who obligates himself by purchasing for sacrifice, he must give the specific animal in charity because the obligation is attached to the physical entity. This is because the poor person's purchase with intention is like a vow. If sacrifice is missed due to time passing, charity replaces it, analogous to missing Jumu'ah and praying Zuhr. The passage ends with notes on the commentary's purpose and the inclusion of buffalo and crossbreeds.

Key Terms
جذع (jadha'): A sheep that has completed six months, according to the Hanafi jurists, provided it is large enough to be mistaken for a thani from a distance.
ثني (thani): For sheep/goats: one year old; for cows: two years; for camels: five years.
ضأن (dha'n): Sheep with a tail, as opposed to goats (ma'z).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Six months, provided it is large
C) Two years
D) Five years

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits a jadha' sheep of six months if large; all other animals must be thani. If sacrifice is missed, charity replaces it based on the nature of the obligation.

Valid and Invalid Defects in the Sacrificial Animal
Lists defects that prevent validity of the sacrificial animal

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify which defects invalidate a sacrificial animal (udhiyah) and state the Hanafi ruling for each defect.

Core Idea
Hornless, castrated, and mad animals are valid; blind, one-eyed, emaciated, and lame are not.

Sacrificing an animal (udhiyah) is a sunnah mu'akkadah in the Hanafi school. The validity of the sacrifice depends on the animal's health and freedom from certain defects. This passage from the commentary on al-Wiqayah lists the defects that do and do not invalidate the sacrifice, distinguishing between minor imperfections that are tolerated and serious disabilities that prevent the animal from being offered.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Udhiyah is sunnah mu'akkadah. The passage defines acceptable defects for the animal.
This ruling is from the Hanafi school.
2
List the valid and invalid defects
Valid: hornless (jamma'), castrated (makhsi), mad (thawla'). Invalid: completely blind (a'mya'), one-eyed ('awra'), extremely emaciated ('ajfa'), lame that cannot walk to the slaughter place ('arja').
Madness does not invalidate because the animal can still be slaughtered and produce meat.
3
Understand the definitions
Each defect has a specific definition: jamma' means no horns; makhsi means castrated; thawla' means insane but can graze; a'mya' means no eyes; 'awra' means one eye; 'ajfa' means extremely thin; 'arja' means lame and cannot walk to the place of slaughter.
The condition for lameness is it must prevent walking to the slaughter place.
4
Apply the ruling to practical selection
When choosing an animal for udhiyah, check for these defects. A hornless or castrated sheep is acceptable, but a blind or one-eyed sheep is not. A lame sheep that can still walk to the slaughter area is acceptable; if it cannot walk, it is invalid.
These rules ensure the sacrifice is sound and fulfills the sunnah.

Such as the hornless, the castrated, and the mad, excluding the blind, the one-eyed, the emaciated, and the lame that cannot walk to the place of sacrifice. (Such as the hornless, the castrated, and the mad, excluding the blind, the one-eyed, the emaciated, and the lame that cannot walk to the place of sacrifice). Then commentary on defects: 'blind' means no eyes at all; 'emaciated' is thin; 'lame' is limping; 'cannot walk to the place of sacrifice' means cannot reach the slaughter place. Then on 'thawla' meaning insane, because it does not affect the purpose if it can graze.
Source pages p. 254

Commentary
This passage continues the commentary on the chapter of Udhiyah, focusing on physical defects of the sacrificial animal. The matn states that animals which are hornless (jamma'), castrated (makhsi), or mad (thawla') are valid for sacrifice, but those that are blind (a'mya'), one-eyed ('awra'), extremely emaciated ('ajfa'), or lame ('arja') to the extent that they cannot walk to the slaughter place are not valid. The commentator then explains each term: jamma' is without horns; thawla' is insane (but still valid if it can graze); 'awra' means one-eyed. He then digresses into the definitions of 'thani' and the different ages for sheep, cows, and camels, clarifying that 'ibn haul' means one-year-old sheep, 'ibn du'f' means two-year-old cow, and 'ibn khams' means five-year-old camel, with 'zulf' (cloven hoof) for cows/sheep and 'khuff' (padded foot) for camels. Then he returns to defects: 'a'mya' means completely without eyes; 'ajfa' means emaciated (Persian: laghar); 'arja' means lame (Persian: langi); 'la yamshi ila al-mansak' means it cannot walk to the place of slaughter. The passage concludes that thawla' (madness) does not invalidate because the purpose is meat, and if it can graze, it is acceptable.

Key Terms
جماء (jamma'): An animal without horns; valid for sacrifice.
خصي (makhsi): A castrated animal; valid for sacrifice.
ثولاء (thawla'): Mad or insane animal; valid if it can graze and feed itself.
عمياء (a'mya'): Completely blind (no eyes); invalidates sacrifice.
عوراء ('awra'): One-eyed; invalidates sacrifice.
عجفاء ('ajfa'): Extremely emaciated (Persian: laghar); invalidates sacrifice.
عرجاء ('arja'): Lame, cannot walk to the slaughter place; invalidates sacrifice.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Being blind
C) Being hornless
D) Being lame and unable to walk

Key Takeaway
Only specific defects (complete blindness, one eye, extreme emaciation, lameness preventing walking) invalidate the sacrifice; other defects like being hornless, castrated, or mad do not.

Major and Minor Defects in the Udhiya Sacrificial Animal
Lists permissible defects and prohibits severe ones in udhiya.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between major defects that invalidate the udhiya and minor defects that are overlooked, applying the Hanafi principle that only a major defect (fahish) prevents validity.

Core Idea
A udhiya is valid despite minor defects; only a major defect that reduces meat or prevents normal function invalidates.

Sacrificing an animal during Eid al-Adha requires the animal to be free of major defects. In this lesson, we examine the classical Hanafi rulings on which defects disqualify an animal and which are tolerated. The key principle is that the preventing factor is a serious defect, not a minor one, because animals are rarely without small imperfections.

Guided Path
1
Identify the permissible defects
The text lists animals that are acceptable despite certain conditions: hornless (jammā'), castrated (khaṣī), and insane (thawlā'). These are not considered major defects.
Hornless and castrated are common and do not affect meat quality or viability.
2
Identify the prohibited defects
The following defects render the udhiya invalid: total blindness (amyā'), one-eyed with clearly evident one-eyedness (awrā' bayyin 'awrihā), extreme emaciation with no marrow (ajfā'), lameness preventing walking to the slaughter site (arjā'), missing more than one-third of ear/tail/eye/fat tail (according to al-Jami' al-Saghir), jallālah (feeds on filth only), toothless inability to graze (hatmā'), cut/dry udder, missing nose/tail/limb.
Some defects like missing a quarter are disputed; the relied-upon threshold is more than one-third.
3
Understand the compensation of fatness
If the animal is fat and its skin is intact, even defects like missing parts may be overlooked because the intended purpose (meat and skin) is not impaired.
This is a Hanafi concession (istihsan) that relaxes the strict quantitative rule.
4
Apply the hadith evidence
The hadith 'al-'awrā' al-bayyin 'awruhā' (the one-eyed whose one-eyedness is evident) shows that only clearly evident major defects invalidate, implying that minor or non-evident defects are excused.
The phrase 'bayyin' is key: it restricts the rule to evident cases.
5
Apply the principle of major vs minor
The text states that the preventing factor is a major defect (fahish), not a minor one, because animals are rarely free from minor blemishes.
A minor defect is one that does not affect the meat quantity or the animal's ability to survive.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كالجماء والخصي والثولاء دون العمياء، والعوراء، والعجفاء، والعرجاء التي لا تمشي إلى المنسك. قيل: الثنايا ابن حول، وابن ضعف، وابن خمس من ذوي ظلف وخف. الجماء: التي لا قرن لها، والثولاء: المجنونة، والعوراء: ذات عين واحدة. والعجفاء: التي لا تنقى أي ما يكون عجفها إلى حد لا يكون في عظامها نقى أي مخ. والعرجاء: هي التي لها عرج، لا تمشي إلى المنسك وهو المذبح. قد قيدت العجفاء: بأنها لا تنقى. ومقطوع يدها، أو رجلها، وما ذهب أكثر من ثلث أذنها، أو ذنبها أو عينها، أو إليتها، هذه رواية الجامع الصغير، وقيل: الثلث، وقيل: الربع، كانت سميته ولم يتلف جلدها جاز؛ لأنه لا يخل بالمقصود. وقال في تكملة البحر: ولا يجوز: بالحتماء التي لا أسنان لها إن كانت لا تعتلف، وإن كانت تعتلف جاز هو الصحيح، ولا الجلالة: التي تأكل العذراء ولا تأكل غيرها، ولا مقطوعة الضرع، ولا التي لا تستطيع أن ترضع ولدها، ولا التي يبس ضرعها، ولا مقطوعة الأنف والذنب والطرف. كذا في المحيط. وقيد في الحديث العوراء أيضاً، حيث قال: «العوراء البيّن عورها»، والأصل أن المانع فيه هو العيب الفاحش لا اليسير؛ لأن الحيوان قلما يخلو عن يسير العيب، واليسير هو الذي ليس له تأثير في نقصان اللحم. والنقي: بكسر النون وسكون القاف والمخ: بضم الميم وتشديد الخاء المعجمة، كلاهما بالفارسية مغز استخوان. والفرق بين الذنب والإلية أن الإلية تختص بالغنم دون الذنب.
The hornless, castrated, and insane are acceptable, except the blind, one-eyed, emaciated, and lame that cannot walk to the slaughter place. It is said: the 'thaniya' (animals with two incisors fallen) are one-year-old sheep, cattle that are two years old, and camels that are five years old, from cloven-hoofed and padded-foot animals. The hornless is that which has no horn, the insane is the mad, the one-eyed is she with one eye. The emaciated is that which has no marrow, meaning its condition reaches the point that there is no marrow in its bones. The lame is she with a limp, not walking to the slaughter place which is the sacrificial site. The emaciated has been restricted: that it has no marrow. And [an animal] with a cut hand or leg, and that which has more than a third of its ear, tail, eye, or fat tail gone: this is the narration of al-Jami' al-Saghir. And it is said: a third, and it is said: a quarter. If it is fat and its skin is not spoiled, it is permissible, because it does not impair the intended purpose. And it is said in Takmilat al-Bahr: It is not permissible: the toothless that cannot graze on its own; if it can graze, it is permissible, and that is the correct view. Nor the jallala that eats impurities and nothing else; nor the one with cut udder; nor the one that cannot suckle its young; nor the one with dry udder; nor the one with cut nose, tail, or limb. This is stated in al-Muhit. In the hadith, the one-eyed is also restricted, where he said: 'The one-eyed whose one-eyedness is clearly evident.' And the principle is that the preventing factor is a major defect, not a minor one, because an animal is rarely free from minor defects. The minor defect is one that has no effect on the reduction of meat. And 'al-nuqi' (marrow) is with kasra on the nun and sukun on the qaf, and 'al-mukhkh' is with damm on the mim and shadda on the kha' mu'jama, both meaning in Persian 'bone marrow'. The difference between the tail and the fat-tail is that the fat-tail is specific to sheep, not the tail.
Source pages p. 254

Commentary
This passage is a ruling_with_proof from the classical Hanafi works, mainly al-Jami' al-Saghir and al-Muhit, expanded in the commentary. It begins by listing animals that are acceptable as udhiya despite defects: the hornless (جماء), castrated (خصي), and insane (ثولاء). However, it excludes those with more serious defects: totally blind (عمياء), one-eyed (عوراء), emaciated (عجفاء), and lame that cannot walk to the slaughter site (عرجاء). The passage then defines these terms. The hornless is self-evident; the insane means mad; the one-eyed has one eye; the emaciated has no marrow in bones; the lame has a limp. The condition for emaciation is extreme leanness without marrow. Next, it discusses animals missing parts: a cut hand or leg, or loss of more than a third of the ear, tail, eye, or fat tail. The narration from al-Jami' al-Saghir sets the threshold at more than one-third. Other opinions say one-third or one-quarter. If the animal is fat and its skin intact, it is allowed because the defect does not undermine the purpose (meat and skin). The passage then cites Takmilat al-Bahr prohibiting: the toothless animal that cannot graze on its own (if it can graze, it is allowed), the jallala (animal that only eats filth), the animal with cut udder, unable to suckle young, with dry udder, or cut nose, tail, or limb. This is confirmed in al-Muhit. The hadith about the clearly one-eyed is quoted as evidence that only evident major defects prevent. The underlying principle is that only a major defect (فاحش) that affects meat quantity or animal viability prevents, not a minor one. Minor defects are common and overlooked. The commentary ends with linguistic clarifications: marrow (نقي/مخ) and the distinction between tail (ذنب) and fat-tail (إلية) specific to sheep.

Key Terms
الجماء (al-jammā'): An animal without horns
الخصي (al-khaṣī): Castrated male animal
الثولاء (al-thawlā'): Mad or insane animal
العمياء (al-'amyā'): Totally blind animal (no eyes at all)
العوراء (al-'awrā'): One-eyed animal
العجفاء (al-'ajfā'): Emaciated animal with no marrow in bones
العرجاء (al-'arjā'): Lame animal that cannot walk to the slaughter place
الجلالة (al-jallālah): Animal that eats filth (like human feces) and nothing else
المنسك (al-mansak): The slaughter place or the site of sacrifice
الحتماء (al-ḥatmā'): Toothless animal (can't eat grass on its own)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) A hornless goat that is healthy and fat.
B) A one-eyed sheep that is clearly blind in one eye and very thin.
C) A castrated ram that grazes well and is fat.
D) A cow that has lost a quarter of its tail but is very fat and healthy.

Key Takeaway
Only a major defect that clearly affects the animal's meat or viability invalidates the udhiya; minor imperfections are overlooked.

Major Defects Invalidating Udhiyah
Listing defects that invalidate an udhiyah animal and stating the fāḥish principle

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the major defects (fāḥish) that invalidate an udhiyah animal and apply the principle that only major defects disqualify, while minor defects are overlooked.

Core Idea
Only fāḥish (major) defects invalidate udhiyah; minor defects are overlooked.

Not every imperfection in a sacrificial animal renders it invalid. The Hanafi school distinguishes between major defects that defeat the purpose of sacrifice and minor ones that are practically unavoidable. This passage from ʿUmdat al-Riʿāyah enumerates the specific disqualifying defects and establishes the governing principle: only the fāḥish (grievous) defect matters. Understanding this principle is crucial for correctly selecting a valid udhiyah animal.

Guided Path
1
Identify the explicit defects
Read the list: severed hand/foot, loss of more than one-third of ear, tail, eye, udder; emaciation without marrow; baldness if unable to eat; jallālah; severed udder; inability to suckle; withered udder; severed nose, tail, limb.
The list includes both parts from al-Jāmiʿ al-Ṣaghīr and additions from Takmilat al-Baḥr.
2
Define the severity threshold for emaciation
The term al-ʿajfāʾ is defined as an animal so thin that its bones contain no marrow (nuqay). This sets a clear benchmark for what constitutes fāḥish emaciation.
3
Distinguish fāḥish from minor defects
The text states the general rule: the preventer is the fāḥish (major) defect, not the minor one. A minor defect has no effect on the quantity of meat; the major defect is known by contrast.
Minor defects are excused because animals are rarely free from them.
4
Apply the exception for fat animals
If the animal is fat (samīnah) and its skin is intact, it may be valid despite a defect, because the purpose (meat) is not compromised.
This exception is explicitly mentioned for the severed limb case.
5
Recognize the additional defects from Takmilat al-Baḥr
The commentator adds disqualifying conditions: baldness preventing eating, jallālah (feces-eater), udder defects, and severed extremities. These expand the list beyond the matn.
These are drawn from another source, al-Muḥīṭ.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الأضحية تعريفها وشروطها وأحكامها
ومقطوع يدها ، أو رجلها، وما ذَهَبَ أكثر من ثلث أُذنِها ، أو ذنبها أو عَيْنِها ، أو إليتها
وقد قيدت العجفاء : بأنها لا تنقى : أي ما يكون عجفها إلى حد لا يكون في عظامها نقى أي مخ.
ومقطوع يدها ، أو رجلُها ، وما ذَهَبَ أكثر من ثلث أُذنِها ، أو ذنبها أو عينها، أو إليتها)، هذه رواية «الجامع الصغير)) ، وقيل : الثلث ، وقيل : الربع ، كانت سميته ولم يتلف جلدها جاز ؛ لأنه لا يخل بالمقصود.
وقال في تكملة البحر») : ولا يجوز : بالحتماء التي لا أسنان لها إن كانت لا تعتلف ، وإن كانت تعتلف جاز هو الصحيح، ولا الجلالة : التي تأكل العذراء ولا تأكلُ غيرها، ولا مقطوعة الضرع، ولا التي لا تستطيع أن ترضع ولدها، ولا التي يبس ضرعها، ولا مقطوعة الأنف والذنب والطرف. كذا في «المحيط». 11 ] قوله : وقد قيدت...الخ ؛ أقول : وقد قيد في الحديث العوراء أيضاً، حيث قال : «العوراء البيِّنُ عورها (۳) ، فالأظهر أن لا يتعرض الشارح له إليه أيضاً. واعلم أن الأصل أن المانع فيه هو العيب الفاحش لا اليسير؛ لأن الحيوان قلما يخلو عن يسير العيب، واليسير هو الذي ليس له تأثير في نقصان اللحم، ومنه يعلمُ الفاحش.
والنقي : بكسر النون وسكون القاف والمخ: بضم الميم، وتشديد الخاء المعجمة، كلاهما بالفارسية، مغز استخوان. قاله الجلبي له [۲] قوله : أو ذَنَبها ؛ - بفتحي الذال المعجمة والنون ، معروف، والفرق بينه وبين الإلية أنها تختص بالغنم دونه. قاله الجلبي
وعندهما إن بقي أكثر من النصف أجزاء ، ثم طريق معرفة ذهاب ثلث العين، أن يَشُدَّ العين الماؤفة، فيقرب إليها العلف إذا كانت جائعة ، فينظرُ أنها من أي مكان رأت العلف ، ثُمَّ تشدُّ العين الصحيحة، ويقرِّبُ إليها العَلَف، فينظر أنها من أي مكان رأت العلف، فينظرُ إلى تفاوتِ ما بين المكانين، فإن كان ثلثاً ، فقد ذَهَبَ الثلث، وهكذا.
Book of Sacrifice: Definition, Conditions, and Rulings.
And (the animal) with a severed hand or foot, and that which has lost more than one-third of its ear, or tail, or eye, or udder.
And 'al-ʿajfā' has been restricted: that it is not marrowy: i.e., its emaciation reaches a degree that there is no marrow in its bones.
And (the animal with) a severed hand or foot, and that which has lost more than one-third of its ear, or tail, or eye, or udder: this is the narration of al-Jāmiʿ al-Ṣaghīr. And it is said: one-third, and it is said: one-fourth. If it is fat and its skin is not damaged, it is permissible because it does not defeat the purpose.
And he said in Takmilat al-Baḥr: It is not permissible: the bald (animal) that has no teeth if it cannot eat; if it can eat, it is permissible—that is the correct view. Nor the jallālah: that eats feces and does not eat other food. Nor the one with a severed udder, nor the one that cannot suckle its young, nor the one with a withered udder, nor the one with severed nose, tail, and limb. Thus in al-Muḥīṭ.
His statement: 'And it has been restricted...' I say: In the hadith, the one-eyed is also restricted, where he said: 'The one-eyed whose blindness is obvious.' So it is apparent that the commentator should not have mentioned it also. Know that the basic principle is that the preventer here is the fāḥish (major) defect, not the slight one; because an animal is rarely free from a slight defect. The slight defect is that which has no effect in decreasing the meat, and from that the fāḥish is known.
An-nuqay: with kasrah of the nūn and sukun of the qāf, and al-mukhkh: with ḍammah of the mīm and tashdīd of the khāʾ; both are in Persian: 'marrow of the bone'. Al-Jalabī said. [2] His statement: 'or its tail' – with fatḥah of the dhāl and nūn, it is well-known; the difference between it and the udder is that the latter is specific to sheep without the former. Al-Jalabī said.
And according to them (Abū Yūsuf and Muḥammad), if more than half remains, it suffices. Then the method of knowing the loss of one-third of the eye: one ties the defective eye, then brings fodder near it when it is hungry, then observes from which place it sees the fodder; then one ties the healthy eye, and brings fodder near it, then observes from which place it sees the fodder; then one observes the difference between the two places: if it is one-third, then one-third has gone, and so on.
Source pages p. 255

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement on the defects that disqualify an animal for udhiyah (sacrifice). The author lists specific defects: severed limb, loss of more than one-third of ear, tail, eye, or udder. The severity of emaciation (ʿajfāʾ) is defined as lack of marrow in bones. There is a dispute in transmission: al-Jāmiʿ al-Ṣaghīr mentions one-third, while others say one-fourth. However, if the animal is fat despite the defect, it is allowed because the purpose (meat) is not lost. The commentator adds from Takmilat al-Baḥr: an animal without teeth that cannot eat is invalid; the jallālah (feces-eater) is invalid; also animals with severed udder, inability to suckle, withered udder, or severed nose/tail/limb. The key principle is that only fāḥish (major) defects prevent validity; minor defects are overlooked because animals are rarely free from them. The method to measure loss of vision in the eye involves comparing the visual field of the defective eye with the healthy eye to determine if one-third is lost, matching the threshold mentioned. The phrase 'according to them' refers to the Two Companions (Abū Yūsuf and Muḥammad), indicating that if more than half of a limb remains, the defect is not major. This passage is a commentary expanding on the matn of al-Wiqāyah.

Key Terms
العجفاء (al-ʿajfāʾ): An emaciated animal with no marrow in its bones, indicating extreme thinness.
النقى (an-nuqay): Marrow inside bones; the condition that is absent in a severely emaciated ʿajfāʾ animal.
الجلالة (al-jallālah): An animal that eats feces (ʿadhirāʾ) and refuses other fodder, making its meat undesirable.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is a disqualifying defect for an udhiyah animal?
A) A slight limp that does not affect the meat
B) Loss of more than one-third of the ear
C) Loss of one tooth
D) A small scar on the skin

Key Takeaway
Only fāḥish (major) defects—those that significantly reduce meat or health—invalidate an udhiyah animal; minor defects are excused.

Measuring Eye Defect and the Intra-Hanafi Threshold Dispute
Method for measuring loss of vision and the intra-Hanafi dispute on the threshold

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi method for measuring loss of vision in an udhiyah animal and state the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Two Companions on the threshold for disqualification.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa: loss of more than one-third vision disqualifies; Abu Yusuf and Muhammad: if more than half remains, it suffices.

How do you determine if an eye defect reaches the disqualifying threshold? The commentators of the Hanafi school devised a practical test using the animal's feeding behavior. This lesson unpacks that measurement method and the accompanying intra-Hanafi dispute on whether the threshold is one-third (Abu Hanifa) or one-half (the Two Companions). Understanding this method and dispute is essential for correctly applying the ruling in practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the threshold positions
The passage states: 'And according to them (Abū Yūsuf and Muḥammad), if more than half remains, it suffices.' This implies Abu Hanifa's view is that loss of more than one-third disqualifies, even if more than half remains. The mufta bihi is Abu Hanifa's position.
2
Understand the measurement method for the eye
The method: tie the defective eye, bring feed near the animal when hungry, observe the distance from which it sees the feed. Then tie the healthy eye, bring feed, and observe again. Compare the two distances; the difference indicates the fraction of vision lost.
The method is analogized to other limbs to determine one-third loss.
3
Interpret the result
If the difference between the distances is one-third of the healthy eye's range, then one-third of vision is lost. This matches Abu Hanifa's threshold for disqualification (loss >1/3).
4
Apply the dispute to practical scenarios
Consider a case where the defective eye sees at 6 feet and the healthy eye at 10 feet. Loss = 4/10 = 2/5 = 0.4, which is >1/3, so Abu Hanifa says invalid; but more than half remains (0.6), so Sahibayn say valid.

Source Text

Sacrifice by Co-Owners When One Dies: Istihsan vs Qiyas
Ruling on joint sacrifice when a co-owner dies and heirs authorize

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on joint sacrifice when a co-owner dies and explain how istihsan overrides qiyas in this case.

Core Idea
Sacrifice on behalf of a deceased co-owner is valid by istihsan because worship can benefit the dead.

Seven people jointly buy a cow or camel for udhiyah. One dies before slaughter, and the heirs authorize the remaining six to proceed. Is the sacrifice valid for both the deceased and the survivors? This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute where Abū Yūsuf argues by qiyas that it is invalid, while the majority relies on istihsan to permit it. Understanding the reasoning behind each view sharpens your ability to weigh analogical reasoning against juristic preference.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the legal question
Seven co-owners of a sacrificial animal; one dies. The heirs say: 'Slaughter it on his behalf and on your behalf.' The question is whether this is valid.
The scenario assumes the animal is suitable for multiple shares (cow/camel for seven).
2
State the majority Hanafi position (istihsan)
The relied-upon view (Abū Ḥanīfa and Muḥammad) holds it valid. This is based on istihsan, analogizing to charity on behalf of the deceased, which is a valid act of worship that benefits the dead.
The Prophet (ﷺ) sacrificed on behalf of his entire ummah, showing that sacrifice for others is worship.
3
State Abū Yūsuf's qiyas position
Abū Yūsuf holds it invalid by qiyas. He argues it is a donation by destruction (itlāf) on behalf of another, like manumission on behalf of the deceased, which is invalid because it imposes wala' (clientage).
Manumission creates a legal bond (wala') that involves inheritance rights, which cannot be imposed on the deceased.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response distinguishing sacrifice from manumission
The majority responds that wala' is a worldly right, whereas sacrifice is pure worship without such consequences. Therefore, the analogy to charity (which is purely worship) is stronger than the analogy to manumission.
The key difference is the presence of a worldly right (wala') in manumission, absent in sacrifice.
5
Determine the practical consequence and the muftā bihi
With heirs' permission, the sacrifice is valid and fulfills the obligation for all. Without permission, it is invalid for the survivors. The muftā bihi position is the istihsan view.
Abū Yūsuf's view is not operative for fatwa; the majority position is relied upon.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن مات أحد سبعة ، وقال ورثته : اذبحوها عنه وعنكم صح، كبقرة عن أضحية ومتعة وقران
وعندهما إن بقي أكثر من النصف أجزاء ، ثم طريق معرفة ذهاب ثلث العين، أن يَشُدَّ العين الماؤفة، فيقرب إليها العلف إذا كانت جائعة ، فينظرُ أنها من أي مكان رأت العلف ، ثُمَّ تشدُّ العين الصحيحة، ويقرِّبُ إليها العَلَف، فينظر أنها من أي مكان رأت العلف، فينظرُ إلى تفاوتِ ما بين المكانين، فإن كان ثلثاً ، فقد ذَهَبَ الثلث، وهكذا.
(فإن مات أحد سبعة ، وقال ورثته (۳) : اذبحوها عنه وعنكم صح)، وعن أبي يوسف له أنه لا يصح، وهو القياس؛ لأنه تبرع بالإتلاف ، فلا يجوز عن الغير كالإعتاق عن الميت وجه الاستحسان : أن القربة قد تقع عن الميت كالتصدق بخلاف الإعتاق، فإنّ فيه إلزام الولاء على الميت، كبقرة عن أضحية ومتعة وقران (۱) [١] قوله : فإن مات...الخ ؛ صورة المسألة إذا اشترى سبعة بقرة أو إبلاً ليضحوا بها ، فمات أحدهم قبل النحر ، وقالت الورثة : اذبحوها عنه وعنكم، صح. ووجهه : إنّ البقرة والإبل يجوز عن سبعة ، لكن من شرطه أن يكون قصد الكل القربة، وإن اختلف جهاتها كالأضحية والقرآن والتمتع عندنا؛ لاتحاد المقصود، وهو القربة، وقد وجد هذا الشرط ؛ لأنَّ التضحية عن الغير عرفت قربة.
ألا ترى أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم ضحى عن أمته» (۲)، رواه ابن ماجة عن عائشة رضي الله عنها، وهذا الذي ذكرناه استحسان، والقياس خلافه، وهو رواية عن أبي يوسف الله: كما قال الشارح الله ، وعن أبي يوسف الله : إنه لا يصح، وهو القياس.
:
[٢] قوله : وقال ورثته...الخ ؛ ولو ذبحها الباقون بغير إذن الورثة لا يجزئهم ؛ لأنه لم يقع بعضها قربة ؛ لعدم الإذن منهم، فلم يقع الكل قرية ضرورة عدم التجزء في حق القربة.
If one of seven dies, and his heirs say: 'Slaughter it on his behalf and on your behalf,' it is valid. Like a cow for udhiyah, tamattu', and qiran. And according to them (Abū Yūsuf and Muḥammad), if more than half remains, it suffices. Then the method of knowing the loss of one-third of the eye... (duplicate text omitted in translation).
(If one of seven dies, and his heirs say: 'Slaughter it on his behalf and on your behalf,' it is valid). And from Abū Yūsuf (may Allah have mercy on him) that it is not valid, and that is qiyas; because it is a donation by destruction, so it is not permissible on behalf of another, like manumission on behalf of a deceased person. The basis of istihsan: that an act of worship can occur on behalf of the deceased, like charity – unlike manumission, because it entails imposing wala' on the deceased. Like a cow for udhiyah, tamattu', and qiran. [1] His statement: 'If one dies...' The scenario: if seven people bought a cow or camel to sacrifice, then one of them dies before slaughter, and the heirs say: 'Slaughter it on his behalf and on your behalf,' it is valid. The reason: a cow or camel can be shared by seven, but the condition is that all intend an act of worship, even if the types differ – like udhiyah, qiran, and tamattu' according to us; because the objective is one, which is worship, and this condition is present because sacrificing on behalf of another is known to be an act of worship. Do you not see that the Prophet (peace be upon him) sacrificed on behalf of his entire ummah? (Narrated by Ibn Mājah from ʿĀʾishah). This that we have mentioned is istihsan, and qiyas is contrary to it, and it is a narration from Abū Yūsuf (as the commentator said): it is not valid, and that is qiyas.
[2] His statement: 'And his heirs said...' And if the remaining ones slaughter without the permission of the heirs, it does not suffice them; because a part of it did not occur as an act of worship due to lack of permission, so the whole did not occur as an act of worship due to the necessity that worship cannot be divided.
Source pages p. 256

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the validity of slaughtering a jointly-owned sacrificial animal when one co-owner dies before slaughter. The issue: seven people buy a cow or camel for udhiyah. One dies. The heirs authorize the remaining six to slaughter it on behalf of both the deceased and themselves. According to the relied-upon position (istihsan), this is valid. Abū Yūsuf's qiyas-based opinion holds it invalid. The commentator explains the reasoning: istihsan draws an analogy to charity on behalf of the deceased – an act of worship that benefits the dead. The hadith that the Prophet (ﷺ) sacrificed on behalf of his entire ummah supports that sacrifice for others is a valid worship. Qiyas compares it to manumission (ʿitq) on behalf of the dead, which is invalid because it imposes wala' (clientage) on the deceased, which is a worldly right. Since sacrifice does not entail such imposition, it is valid. The passage also notes that if the remaining partners slaughter without the heirs' permission, the sacrifice does not suffice them (the survivors), because worship cannot be divided without the consent of all parties. This is an expansion (sharḥ) on the matn of al-Wiqāyah, clarifying the legal reasoning and the disagreement with Abū Yūsuf.

Key Terms
الاستحسان (al-istihsan): A method of juristic preference that overrides qiyas in favor of a more equitable ruling; here, it allows the sacrifice on behalf of the deceased.
القياس (al-qiyas): Analogical reasoning; here it is used by Abū Yūsuf to argue that sacrifice on behalf of a dead person is invalid, analogous to manumission.
الولاء (al-walāʾ): Clientage or alliance that arises from manumission; it is a legal bond that imposes inheritance rights, which is why manumission on behalf of a deceased is problematic.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the basis for the Hanafi position allowing sacrifice on behalf of a deceased co-owner by the heirs' permission?
A) Qiyas to manumission
B) Istihsan analogizing to charity on behalf of the deceased
C) Consensus of all scholars
D) The hadith that the Prophet sacrificed for his family only

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school relies on istihsan to permit sacrifice on behalf of a deceased co-owner with heirs' permission, overriding the qiyas analogy to manumission.

Udhiyah for a Deceased Partner: Istihsan vs. Qiyas
Ruling on udhiyah when a partner dies

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on udhiyah when a partner dies and explain the istihsan argument that overrides qiyas.

Core Idea
Udhiyah for a deceased partner is valid by istihsan because piety can be dedicated to the dead, unlike manumission which imposes wala'.

When seven people jointly purchase an animal for udhiyah and one dies before slaughter, a question arises: can the remaining partners slaughter on behalf of the deceased? This lesson unpacks the Hanafi ruling, the qiyas objection raised by Abu Yusuf, and the istihsan reasoning that prevails, supported by the Prophet's practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Seven partners buy a cow or camel for udhiyah. One partner dies before slaughter. The heirs instruct the survivors to slaughter on behalf of the deceased and themselves.
2
State the Hanafi ruling and its basis (istihsan)
The ruling is valid (sahih) by istihsan. The basis: dedicating piety (qurbah) to the deceased is permissible, analogous to charity, and the Prophet himself sacrificed for his ummah.
Istihsan overrides qiyas here.
3
Identify the qiyas objection
Abu Yusuf (in one narration) holds it invalid by qiyas. The analogy: slaughter is a gratuitous destruction of property, so it cannot be performed on behalf of another, just as manumission cannot be on behalf of the deceased.
Qiyas would make the slaughter fasid.
4
Explain the response distinguishing udhiyah from manumission
The Hanafi response: manumission imposes wala' (clientage) on the deceased, which is not purely piety, while udhiyah is pure piety. Therefore the analogy fails, and istihsan, supported by the Prophet's practice, prevails.
The key distinction is the presence of wala' in manumission.
5
Note the evidence (Prophet's practice)
The hadith 'The Prophet sacrificed for his ummah' (Ibn Majah) directly supports the validity of sacrificing on behalf of others without their express will.
This is a dalil naqli reinforcing istihsan.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن مات أحد سبعة ، وقال ورثته : اذبحوها عنه وعنكم صح، كبقرة عن أضحية ومتعة وقران وعندهما إن بقي أكثر من النصف أجزاء ، ثم طريق معرفة ذهاب ثلث العين، أن يَشُدَّ العين الماؤفة، فيقرب إليها العلف إذا كانت جائعة ، فينظرُ أنها من أي مكان رأت العلف ، ثُمَّ تشدُّ العين الصحيحة، ويقرِّبُ إليها العَلَف، فينظر أنها من أي مكان رأت العلف، فينظرُ إلى تفاوتِ ما بين المكانين، فإن كان ثلثاً ، فقد ذَهَبَ الثلث، وهكذا. (فإن مات أحد سبعة ، وقال ورثته : اذبحوها عنه وعنكم صح)، وعن أبي يوسف له أنه لا يصح، وهو القياس؛ لأنه تبرع بالإتلاف ، فلا يجوز عن الغير كالإعتاق عن الميت وجه الاستحسان : أن القربة قد تقع عن الميت كالتصدق بخلاف الإعتاق، فإنّ فيه إلزام الولاء على الميت، كبقرة عن أضحية ومتعة وقران [١] قوله : فإن مات...الخ ؛ صورة المسألة إذا اشترى سبعة بقرة أو إبلاً ليضحوا بها ، فمات أحدهم قبل النحر ، وقالت الورثة : اذبحوها عنه وعنكم، صح. ووجهه : إنّ البقرة والإبل يجوز عن سبعة ، لكن من شرطه أن يكون قصد الكل القربة، وإن اختلف جهاتها كالأضحية والقرآن والتمتع عندنا؛ لاتحاد المقصود، وهو القربة، وقد وجد هذا الشرط ؛ لأنَّ التضحية عن الغير عرفت قربة. ألا ترى أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم ضحى عن أمته» (۲)، رواه ابن ماجة عن عائشة رضي الله عنها، وهذا الذي ذكرناه استحسان، والقياس خلافه، وهو رواية عن أبي يوسف الله: كما قال الشارح الله ، وعن أبي يوسف الله : إنه لا يصح، وهو القياس. [٢] قوله : وقال ورثته...الخ ؛ ولو ذبحها الباقون بغير إذن الورثة لا يجزئهم ؛ لأنه لم يقع بعضها قربة ؛ لعدم الإذن منهم، فلم يقع الكل قرية ضرورة عدم التجزء في حق القربة.
If one of seven dies and his heirs say: slaughter it for him and for you, it is valid, like a cow for udhiyah, tamattu', and qiran. According to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), if more than half remains, it suffices. Then the method of knowing the loss of one-third of the eye: bind the affected eye, bring fodder near it when it is hungry, and observe from which place it sees the fodder. Then bind the healthy eye, bring fodder near it, and observe from which place it sees the fodder. Then look at the difference between the two places; if it is one-third, then one-third has gone, and so on. (If one of seven dies and his heirs say: slaughter it for him and for you, it is valid). And from Abu Yusuf that it is not valid, and that is qiyas; because it is a gratuitous destruction, so it is not valid on behalf of another like manumission on behalf of the deceased. The istihsan is that piety can be performed on behalf of the deceased like charity, unlike manumission because it imposes wala' on the deceased, like a cow for udhiyah, tamattu', and qiran. [1] His saying: 'If one dies...' etc.; the scenario: if seven purchased a cow or camel to sacrifice with it, and one of them dies before slaughter, and the heirs say: slaughter it for him and for you, it is valid. The reason: a cow and camel are permissible for seven, but the condition is that all intend piety, even if their modes differ like udhiyah, qiran, and tamattu' according to us, because the objective is one, i.e., piety, and this condition exists because sacrificing on behalf of another is known to be piety. Do you not see that the Prophet (peace be upon him) sacrificed for his ummah? (Reported by Ibn Majah from A'ishah). This is istihsan, and qiyas is contrary, and it is a narration from Abu Yusuf as the commentator said, and from Abu Yusuf that it is not valid, and it is qiyas. [2] His saying: 'and his heirs say' etc.; if the remaining slaughter without the permission of the heirs, it does not suffice them, because part of it did not become piety due to lack of permission, so all of it did not become piety due to the impossibility of partibility in matters of piety.
Source pages p. 256

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the book of udhiyah. It addresses a scenario where seven people jointly purchase a sacrificial animal, and one of them dies before the slaughter. The matn states that if the heirs of the deceased instruct the surviving partners to slaughter the animal on behalf of both the deceased and themselves, the sacrifice is valid. This is analogized to a cow or camel that suffices for seven even when the intentions differ (udhiyah, tamattu', qiran) because the common objective is piety. The commentator then discusses two points: firstly, that according to Abu Yusuf (in one narration), this is invalid based on qiyas, because slaughtering is a gratuitous destruction of property, and gratuitous acts cannot be performed on behalf of others, like manumission on behalf of a deceased person. However, the relied-upon position (istihsan) is that it is valid, because piety can be performed on behalf of the deceased, as seen in charity. The difference is that manumission imposes the obligation of wala' (clientage) on the deceased, which is not a form of piety, whereas slaughtering for udhiyah is pure piety. The Prophet's practice is cited as evidence. Secondly, the commentator notes that if the surviving partners slaughter without the heirs' permission, the sacrifice is not valid because the deceased's share was not intended for piety. Also, the passage includes a brief method for determining loss of one-third of the eye's vision, which is a separate topic from the book of diyat. The method involves comparing the range of vision with the affected and healthy eyes when fodder is presented to a hungry animal. This interpolation is likely a scribal insertion.

Key Terms
الاستحسان (al-istihsan): Juristic preference; abandoning qiyas in favor of a stronger evidence or maslaha.
القياس (al-qiyas): Analogic deduction; applying the ruling of an original case to a new case based on a common effective cause.
الولاء (al-wala'): Clientage; the legal relationship established upon manumission, entitling the former master to inherit from the freed slave.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The deceased's heirs have ownership over his share.
B) Slaughtering for the deceased is analogous to giving charity on his behalf, which is permissible.
C) The animal is jointly owned, so the survivors can sacrifice for all.
D) Abu Yusuf later retracted his opinion.

Key Takeaway
Udhiyah on behalf of a deceased partner is valid by istihsan when heirs consent, based on the Prophet's practice and the principle that piety can be dedicated to the dead.

Eating and Distributing Udhiyah Meat
States the ruling on consumption and recommended charity from udhiyah meat

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on eating and distributing udhiyah meat, and distinguish between a regular udhiyah and one made obligatory by vow.

Core Idea
Eating from the udhiyah is permitted; giving one-third in charity is recommended, but a vowed udhiyah must be fully given in charity.

This passage from the book of Udhiyah clarifies the rulings on consumption and distribution of the sacrificial meat. It addresses two key issues: the invalidity if a partner lacks pious intention, and the owner's options for eating, gifting, and giving charity. Understanding these rules ensures the sacrifice fulfills its spiritual purpose.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two main sections
Locate the two distinct rulings: (1) conditions for a valid joint sacrifice, and (2) permissions regarding consuming and distributing the meat.
The passage begins with a condition about partners, then transitions to consumption rules.
2
Analyze the partnership condition
Understand that if any partner is a disbeliever or intends only to eat meat (not piety), the sacrifice is invalid for all. The animal is indivisible in terms of piety.
This ruling is from al-Hidayah.
3
Distinguish regular vs. vowed udhiyah
For a regular udhiyah (wajib or sunnah), eating, gifting, and charity are allowed. For a vowed udhiyah (made obligatory by nadhr), the owner cannot eat or feed the rich; it must all be given in charity.
This distinction is critical and a common source of confusion.
4
Note the recommended division into thirds
The recommended practice is to divide the meat into three parts: one-third to eat, one-third to store, and one-third to give in charity. However, keeping all is permissible.
Evidence from Quranic verses: 'So eat from them and store' (22:36) and 'feed the contented and the beggar' (22:36).
5
Apply the ruling
Given a specific scenario, determine whether the owner can eat, gift, or must give in charity based on whether the udhiyah is vowed or not.
Practice with the exercises below.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الأضحية تعريفها وشروطها وأحكامها وإن كان أحدهم كافراً ، أو مريد اللحم لا ، ويأكل منها ويؤكلُ ويَهَبُ مَن يشاء ، ونُدِبَ التصدق بثلثها وتركه لذي وإن كان أحدهم كافراً ، أو مريد اللحم لا ) ؛ لأن البعض ليس بقربة وهي لا تتجزأ. [۲] [٤] ( ويأكل منها ويؤكلُ ويَهَبُ مَن يشاء ، ونُدِبَ التصدق بثلثها [٤] 11 ] قوله : وإن كان أحدهم كافراً أو مريداً للحم لا ؛ أي لا تجزأ عن واحد منهم ؛ لأن شرط الجواز أن يكون قصداً لكلّ قربة، ولم يوجد ؛ لأنَّ الكافر ليس من أهلها ، وكذا قصد اللحم ينا في القرية، وإذا لم يقع البعض قربة، والإراقة تتجزأ في حق القربة ، لم يقع الكل أيضاً، فامتنع الجواز من «الهداية»(۱).
