The book of Udhiyah: Its definition, conditions, and rulings. And if one of them is a disbeliever, or one who intends meat, it is not valid. And he may eat from it and give to eat and gift to whomever he wishes, and it is recommended to give one-third in charity and leave it for [the poor]. And if one of them is a disbeliever or intends meat, it is not valid; because part is not piety and it is not divisible. [2] [4] (And he may eat from it and give to eat and gift to whomever he wishes, and it is recommended to give one-third in charity) [4] 11] His saying: 'And if one of them is a disbeliever or intends meat, it is not valid'; meaning it does not suffice for any of them; because the condition for validity is that all intend piety, and this is not found; because the disbeliever is not worthy of piety, and likewise the intention of meat contradicts piety. And if part is not piety, and the slaughter is not divisible in terms of piety, then the whole is also not piety, so validity is prevented, from al-Hidayah. (2) His saying: 'And he may eat...' etc.; this applies to both obligatory and sunnah udhiyah if it is not obligatory by vow. If it is obligatory by vow, then the owner may not eat any of it, nor feed a rich person, whether the one who vowed is rich or poor; because its purpose is charity, and the one giving charity may not eat from his charity nor feed the rich; if he eats, he must pay the value of what he ate. Said by al-Zayla'i. [3] His saying: 'to eat and gift' etc.; I say: the first refers to the permissibility of feeding the poor, and the second to the rich, as is clear. And some commentators of al-Wiqayah have stated the opening of the letter kaf in 'yu'kal' (it is eaten) based on the absence of verbs from the root of eating. Said by al-Jalabi. [4] His saying: 'and it is recommended to give one-third in charity'; because the aspects are three: eating and storing, due to His saying: 'So eat from them and store'; and feeding, due to His saying: 'And feed the contented and the beggar.' So it is divided into thirds. He said in al-Bada'i': The best is to give one-third in charity, make one-third a feast for relatives and friends, and store one-third. It is recommended to eat from it. If he keeps all for himself, it is permissible, because the piety lies in the slaughter, and giving in charity of the meat is voluntary.
Source pages p. 257

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from the book of udhiyah, covering two main issues: (1) the invalidity of the sacrifice if one of the seven partners is a disbeliever or intends to eat the meat solely for consumption, and (2) the recommended distribution of the meat. The text first explains that if any partner is a disbeliever (who does not intend piety) or intends only to eat the meat (without the intention of sacrifice), the sacrifice is not valid for any of the partners. The reason is that the animal is not divisible in terms of piety; if one part is not for piety, the whole is invalid. This is taken from al-Hidayah. The second part deals with the consumption of the meat. The owner may eat from the udhiyah, gift it to others (both poor and rich), and it is recommended to give one-third in charity. The commentary explains that this applies to udhiyah that is either sunnah or wajib (not by vow). If the udhiyah is made obligatory by a vow (nadhr), the owner may not eat any of it nor feed a rich person; it must be given entirely in charity. If the owner eats, he must pay the equivalent value. The recommendation of one-third for charity is derived from Quranic verses: 'So eat from them and store' (Surah al-Hajj, 36) and 'And feed the contented and the beggar.' Thus, the meat is to be divided into three parts: eating, storing, and giving in charity. Al-Bada'i' suggests the best practice is to give one-third in charity, use one-third to feed relatives and friends, and store one-third. It is recommended to eat from it, but if one keeps all, it is still permissible because the essential act of piety is the slaughter itself, and charity of the meat is supererogatory.

Key Terms
الأضحية (al-udhiyah): The sacrificial animal slaughtered on the days of Eid al-Adha for piety.
النذر (al-nadhr): A vow making an act obligatory. If udhiyah is vowed, it becomes wajib with stricter rules.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) The owner must give all meat to the poor.
D) The owner may only eat if he is poor.

Key Takeaway
For a regular udhiyah, eating and gifting are permitted and giving charity is recommended; for a vowed udhiyah, the owner cannot eat or feed the rich.

Ruling on Partnership with a Kafir or One Seeking Meat
Explanation of why sacrifice is invalid with a kafir partner

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a shared udhiyah when one partner is a kafir or seeks meat, and explain the rational proof (dalil aqli) behind it.

Core Idea
A shared sacrifice is invalid if any partner lacks the intention of worship, because the act is indivisible.

This lesson examines a key condition for the validity of a shared udhiyah. The Hanafi school holds that if one partner is a disbeliever or participates solely for the meat, the entire sacrifice is invalid. We will explore the reasoning from al-Hidayah, focusing on the condition of intention and the rational proof that the act cannot be partially worship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is a shared udhiyah (sacrifice) where one partner is a non-Muslim (kafir) or participates solely for the meat. The ruling: it is invalid (batil) for all partners.
The ruling is from al-Hidayah.
2
Locate the condition (shart)
The text states the condition: each partner must intend worship (qurbah). This is a prerequisite for validity.
From the text: 'لأن شرط الجواز أن يكون قصداً لكلّ قربة'
3
Understand the rational proof (dalil aqli)
The author argues: (1) The kafir cannot intend worship, and the meat-seeker does not; (2) The act of slaughter cannot be divided into worship and non-worship; (3) Therefore, the whole act is invalid. This is a rational proof based on the indivisibility of the act.
This is a dalil aqli, not a textual proof.
4
Apply the ruling to a scenario
If a group shares an animal, and one is a Muslim but only wants the meat, the entire sacrifice is invalid because the condition of intention is not met for all.
The presence of even one partner lacking intention spoils the whole.
5
Confirm the source and authority
This ruling is from al-Hidayah, a foundational text of the Hanafi school (Zahir al-Riwayah), and it is the relied-upon position.
Zahir al-Riwayah is the highest authority level in the school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن كان أحدهم كافراً، أو مريد اللحم لا؛ أي لا تجزأ عن واحد منهم؛ لأن شرط الجواز أن يكون قصداً لكلّ قربة، ولم يوجد؛ لأنَّ الكافر ليس من أهلها، وكذا قصد اللحم ينا في القرية [؟]، وإذا لم يقع البعض قربة، والإراقة تتجزأ في حق القربة، لم يقع الكل أيضاً، فامتنع الجواز من «الهداية».
And if one of them is a disbeliever, or one desiring the meat, it is not [valid]; i.e., it does not suffice for any one of them, because the condition of permissibility is that each intends worship, and that is not found; because the disbeliever is not of its people, and likewise the intention of meat [?] in the village, and if a part is not worship, and the slaughter cannot be divided in respect of worship, then the whole does not occur either, so permissibility is prevented. From al-Hidayah.
Source pages p. 257

Commentary
This passage is a ruling from al-Hidayah explaining the condition for the validity of a shared udhiyah. If one partner is a kafir or participates solely for the meat, the sacrifice is invalid for all. The reasoning is that the act must be purely for worship; the kafir cannot intend worship, and the one seeking meat is not doing so. Since the sacrifice cannot be partially worship and partially not, it all becomes invalid.

Key Terms
أضحية (udhiyah): The sacrificial animal slaughtered on Eid al-Adha as an act of worship.
قربة (qurbah): An act of worship that brings one closer to Allah, which must be intended for the sacrifice to be valid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a shared udhiyah, if one of the partners is a kafir, what is the ruling according to the Hanafi school?
A) The sacrifice is valid for the Muslim partners only.
B) The entire sacrifice is invalid.
C) The sacrifice is valid if the kafir did not intend worship.
D) The kafir's share is void but the rest is valid.

Key Takeaway
The entire shared sacrifice is invalid if any partner lacks the intention of worship, because the act is indivisible in terms of qurbah.

Recommended Uses of Udhiyah Meat
Rulings on consumption, gifting, and charity of sacrifice meat.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the recommended allocations of udhiyah meat and apply the rule of dividing into thirds.

Core Idea
It is recommended to give one third of udhiyah meat in charity and keep the rest for family and gifts.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah clarifies the recommended (mandub) practices for handling the meat of a voluntary sacrifice (udhiyah). Many assume all must be given away, but the school advises a balanced approach: eat, give gifts, and donate a portion to charity, especially providing for one's dependents.

Guided Path
1
Identify the permitted and recommended actions
The text states that the owner may eat, feed others, and gift the meat (mubah). Charity (sadaqah) is specifically recommended (mandub) for one third of the meat.
The phrase 'nudiba' indicates a recommended act, not obligatory.
2
Understand the recommended division
Though not explicitly stated as thirds, the instruction to give one third in charity implies a practical division: one third charity, one third gifts, and one third for family consumption.
This balance fulfills the sunnah and avoids waste.
3
Consider the family's needs
The text adds that leaving the meat for a person with dependents (dhi 'iyal) is recommended to expand provision for them. This prioritizes family welfare.
The term 'tawsi'at' (expansion) shows the ethical dimension.
4
Apply the ruling in practice
When slaughtering an udhiyah, allocate roughly one third for charity, one third for gifts (including to non-poor), and keep the rest for your household. This is the balanced approach commended by the school.
The ruling applies to voluntary udhiyah, not obligatory (vowed) sacrifices which may have different rules.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويأكل منها ويؤكلُ ويَهَبُ مَن يشاء، ونُدِبَ التصدق بثلثها وتركه لذي عيال؛ توسعة عليهم
And he eats from it, and it is eaten, and he gives to whomever he wishes, and charity of one third of it is recommended, and leaving it for one with a family [is recommended] as an expansion for them.
Source pages p. 257

Commentary
This passage states the recommended practices regarding the meat of the udhiyah (when not vowed). The owner may eat from it, feed others, and give gifts. It is recommended to give one third in charity and to keep some for one's family, especially if they are not well-off. The justification is balancing three purposes: eating, storing, and feeding others, as derived from the Quran and hadith.

Key Terms
ندب (nudiba): It is recommended but not obligatory; an act whose performance is rewarded but omission is not sinful.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the recommended (mandub) action regarding the meat of an udhiyah?
A) Give all of it in charity.
B) Eat it all alone.
C) Give one third in charity, eat some, and give some as gifts.
D) Only give to the poor.

Key Takeaway
It is recommended to give one third of voluntary udhiyah meat in charity, while the rest may be eaten and gifted, with priority given to family provision.

Slaughtering the Udhiyah: Personal or by Proxy
Preference for slaughtering personally or appointing another

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on who should slaughter the udhiyah and explain the ruling when a Kitabi performs the slaughter.

Core Idea
Slaughter the udhiyah yourself if skilled; if not, appoint a Muslim; a Kitabi's slaughter is disliked.

This lesson clarifies the preferred method for slaughtering the udhiyah. The source text provides a clear ruling: the owner should slaughter personally if competent, otherwise delegate to another Muslim. However, the text also addresses a special case—when a Kitabi (a Christian or Jew) performs the slaughter, it is makruh (disliked). Understanding this ruling helps you fulfil this act of worship correctly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its default ruling
The act is slaughtering the udhiyah. The default ruling: it is sunnah muakkadah for the owner to slaughter it himself if he is skilled in the proper method.
This is based on the Prophet's practice.
2
Identify the alternative if not skilled
If the owner is not skilled, he should command another Muslim to perform the slaughter. This is permissible and recommended.
The text says 'illa amara ghayrahu' (otherwise he should command another).
3
Identify the ruling for a Kitabi
The text explicitly states that it is makruh (disliked) for a Kitabi to slaughter the udhiyah, even if appointed by the owner.
This is because udhiyah is an act of worship, and a non-Muslim's involvement reduces its devotional aspect.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والذبح بيده إن أحسن، وإلا أمر غيره، وكره إن ذبحها كتابي والذبح بيده إن أحسن، وإلا أمر غيره، وكره إن ذبحها كتابي
And slaughtering with his own hand if he is skilled, otherwise he should command another; and it is disliked if a Kitabi slaughters it.
Source pages p. 258

Commentary
This passage provides guidance on who should perform the slaughter. If the owner is skilled, it is recommended he slaughter personally. If not, he may ask another Muslim to do so. The Prophet (peace be upon him) demonstrated this by slaughtering most of his animals himself. However, it is disliked for a Kitabi (Christian or Jew) to slaughter the udhiyah, even if the owner appoints them, because it is an act of worship. Some Hanafi scholars, however, consider it permissible without dislike if done by the owner's command.

Key Terms
كتابي (Kitabi): A person of the Book (Christian or Jew) who is acknowledged as having a revealed scripture.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi ruling on having a Kitabi slaughter one's udhiyah?
A) It is absolutely forbidden.
B) It is disliked (makruh).
C) It is recommended.
D) It is obligatory to have a Muslim do it.

Key Takeaway
For udhiyah, slaughter yourself if capable; if not, appoint a Muslim; a Kitabi's slaughter is disliked but not invalid.

Kitabi Slaughter of Udhiyah: Dislike or Permissibility?
Analysis of intra-Hanafi dispute on Kitabi slaughter of udhiyah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding Kitabi slaughter of udhiyah and state the later relied-upon position.

Core Idea
A Kitabi can slaughter udhiyah by deputyship; the dispute is whether the owner's command removes the dislike.

This lesson examines a subtle intra-Hanafi disagreement about the slaughter of the sacrificial animal (udhiyah) by a Kitabi (People of the Book). While the basic permissibility of the slaughter itself is accepted, the issue is whether it remains disliked (makruh) when the Muslim owner commands the Kitabi. Understanding the reasoning will clarify the Hanafi approach to deputyship in worship.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the two views within the Hanafi school on Kitabi slaughter: the earlier view holds it disliked even when commanded; the later view holds it permissible without dislike when commanded.
The later position is now mufta bihi.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
The opponent is the earlier Hanafi scholars (e.g., Takmilat al-Bahr) who consider it disliked because the Kitabi lacks intention for worship.
This is not an inter-madhhab dispute but within the Hanafi school.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
The evidence: udhiyah is a worship (qurbah), and the Kitabi is not qualified for worship because he lacks the required intention (niyyah).
The focus is on the Kitabi's personal qualification for worship.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
Later scholars (al-Zayla'i, author of Radd al-Muhtar) argue that the Muslim's command constitutes deputyship (niyaba), and the worship is realized through the Muslim's intention, not the Kitabi's. The Kitabi is merely the executor of dhabh, for which he is qualified.
The response refines the concept of deputyship.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: if a Muslim commands a Kitabi, some consider it makruh, others consider it permissible without dislike. Fatwa follows the latter.
The tarjih is based on the strength of deputyship reasoning.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكره إن ذبحها كتابي [٣] قوله : وكره أن ذبحها كتابي...الخ ؛ في تكملة البحر») : وكره ذبح الكتابي ؛ لأنه قربة، وهو ليس من أهلها، ولو أمره فذبح جاز ؛ لأنه من أهل الذكاة، والقربة أقيمت بإنابته. وفي رد المحتار) : وظاهرُ كلامِ الزَّيْلَعِي (٦) وغيره عدم الكراهة لو كان بأمره ، و به صرح مسكين مستدلاً عليه بقول «الكافي» : ولو أمر المسلم كتابياً بأن يذبح أضحيته
And it is disliked if a Kitabi slaughters it. He said: 'And it is disliked that a Kitabi slaughters it... In Takmilat al-Bahr: It is disliked for a Kitabi to slaughter because it is an act of worship, and he is not qualified for it; if he is ordered and then slaughters, it is permissible because he is qualified for dhabh (ritual slaughter), and the worship is fulfilled by his deputyship. In Radd al-Muhtar: The apparent statement of al-Zayla'i and others is that there is no dislike if it is by his command, and Maskeen stated this, citing al-Kafi: If a Muslim orders a Kitabi to slaughter his udhiyah...'
Source pages p. 258

Commentary
This passage addresses the difference within the Hanafi school regarding slaughter by a Kitabi. The primary position is that it is makruh because udhiyah is a worship and the Kitabi is not qualified for worship. However, if the Muslim explicitly orders the Kitabi to slaughter, some scholars (like al-Zayla'i) hold that it is not makruh, since the Kitabi is capable of valid dhabh and acts as the Muslim's deputy. This is the view adopted in later fatwa works like Radd al-Muhtar.

Key Terms
كراهة (karahah): Dislike; an act that is not sinful but better to avoid. In this context, it is likely makruh tanzihi.
كتابي (kitabi): A person from the People of the Book (Jewish or Christian).
أضحية (udhiyah): The sacrificial animal slaughtered on Eid al-Adha.
إنابة (inabah / niyaba): Deputyship; appointing someone else to perform an act on one's behalf.
ذكاة (tadhkiyah / dhabh): Ritual slaughter according to Islamic law.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the later relied-upon Hanafi position, what is the ruling if a Muslim asks a Kitabi to slaughter his udhiyah?
A) It is forbidden.
B) It is disliked.
C) It is permissible without dislike.
D) It is invalid.

Key Takeaway
The later Hanafi position is that a Kitabi slaughtering udhiyah by the Muslim's command is valid and not disliked, due to valid deputyship.
